offices say contravene the Fourth Geneva Convention and risk entrenching the occupation [1026][986][1048]. Palestinian authorities
publicly condemned specific new unit approvals (e.g., 126 units in Jenin at end-April 2026) and requested international action, while UN
officials warned of rapidly expanding settlement activity including plans to build more than 1,000 settlement units within short
timeframes [1059][1058].
Diplomatic tracks and mediation initiatives remain active but contested: a Palestinian-drafted roadmap demanding international
forces, governance transfer, and reconstruction was advanced in April 2026 but reportedly rejected by US and Israeli interlocutors,
leaving legal and political implementation mechanisms unresolved [995]. The Palestinian Ministry of Public Works and Housing signed
a five-year memorandum of understanding with UNOPS to support infrastructure recovery, resource mobilization, and reconstruction
planning in Gaza and the West Bank [975]. Palestinian authorities have also engaged EU and UN envoys to accelerate implementation
of Resolution 2803 and transitional governance arrangements, publicly demanding urgent international action including sanctions
and enforcement of international law [1058][1027]. UN experts have warned that large-scale reconstruction — estimated at over US$71
billion in the joint UN/EU/World Bank assessment — will fail unless legal safeguards, Palestinian participation, and an end to
occupation-related constraints are incorporated into reconstruction processes [967][988][994].
Humanitarian Impact of Legislation
Gaza
Legislative and policy decisions have had direct and severe consequences for humanitarian access and civilian welfare. Israeli
operational control has been extended to movement rules inside Gaza through designated coordination zones (the so-called "orange
line"), which require aid actors to coordinate movements with the military and have contributed to areas becoming effectively
inaccessible for civilians and humanitarians; at least three Palestinians working with foreign aid organizations were killed in the area
between these lines since mid-March [1010]. MSF documented long-standing denials of critical WASH and other lifesaving supplies —
including a reported denial of all MSF requests through the Israeli-controlled approval system since 1 January 2026 — and noted
restricted electricity and fuel essential for water treatment since October 2023 [971][1041]. UN briefings and operational reports
document deadly strikes on water points, the suspension of work at key filling sites after staff were killed, and estimates that around
60% of families lack adequate access to clean water, with trucking and temporary measures described as unsustainable [984].
17
WHO and UN briefings documented a sharp rise in attacks on health infrastructure and personnel, with WHO reporting 149 attacks on
the health sector resulting in 100 deaths and 233 injuries, highlighting persistent violations of protections for medical services under IHL
[984]. Only 296 of 683 health service points were functioning, and just 23 were fully operational, while limited medical evacuations
continued through Rafah [1049]. Humanitarian personnel face escalating threats more broadly, with a sharp rise in aid-worker
fatalities across Gaza and the West Bank, including hundreds of humanitarian deaths reported in 2025 alone, signalling a collapse of
protection for aid workers [1001][1007].
Restrictions on movement, a collapsing permit system, and routine access denials have also eroded labour rights and livelihoods: the
number of Palestinian workers inside Israel and pre-war settlements fell to approximately 51,000 in Q4 2025, and monitors recorded
roughly 2,000 traffic restrictions in 2025 limiting access to work and services [985][981]. Financial and institutional constraints
compound these operational barriers — Israeli measures including the withholding of clearance revenues and restrictions on the entry
of goods have been reported to undermine Palestinian national institutions and impede relief, recovery, and reconstruction efforts, a
concern raised publicly by the Palestinian prime minister on 28 April 2026 [1040][1027]. The joint UN/EU/World Bank damage and needs
assessment estimated reconstruction needs at more than $71 billion, noted massive housing destruction, and the displacement of
approximately 1.9 million people, warning that reconstruction cannot succeed without addressing continuing occupation-related
restrictions that shape access, rights, and accountability [967][992][988].
International Agreements Impacting the Crisis
Gaza
The UN Security Council-endorsed Gaza Peace Plan (Resolution 2803/2025) remains the central international framework for the crisis,
calling for the establishment of a temporary International Stabilization Force in Gaza and unhindered humanitarian access. An
EU–ASEAN joint statement on 28 April 2026 urged full compliance with the ceasefire and relevant UNSC provisions [1019][1018].
Palestinian authorities have publicly demanded urgent implementation of Resolution 2803 and transitional governance arrangements,
engaging EU and UN envoys toward this end and calling for sanctions and enforcement of international law [1058][1027].
Compliance with humanitarian provisions under the ceasefire protocol has been weak in practice: the agreed entry of 600 trucks per
day has been met at only approximately 39% of that volume, and fuel deliveries have reached roughly 14.9% of required quantities,
disrupting electricity, water, and sanitation services [966]. Attempts to bypass the blockade by sea have been intercepted, with flotilla
vessels boarded, crews detained or deported, and activists prevented from delivering aid [976][1006][996].
NGOs including MSF have called on UN Member States to uphold IHL, implement obligations referenced in the 2024 ICJ advisory
opinion, and pressure Israeli authorities to cease impeding water, sanitation, and hygiene services in Gaza [971]. The joint UN/EU/World
Bank assessment estimated overall reconstruction needs at approximately $71.4 billion, with $26.3 billion required for the first 18
months, identifying a major recovery financing gap [988][994]. Key governance and legal gaps persist in reconstruction planning: UN
experts have been criticized for failing to specify the conditions, oversight mechanisms, or rights-based safeguards — including
Palestinian-led, transparent governance — required before reconstruction can proceed, leaving donors reluctant and creating a risk of
profit-driven or exclusionary rebuilding [967][992][975].
Limitations of Current Policies
Gaza
Existing legal and policy frameworks suffer from critical implementation gaps that have compounded the humanitarian crisis. The
scale of destruction is immense: more than 371,000 housing units have been destroyed or damaged in Gaza, approximately 1.9 million
people have been displaced, and over 60% of the population remain homeless [967][992][988]. Water, sanitation, and hygiene
systems have largely collapsed — Gazans sometimes receive less than 6 litres of water per person per day, over 90% of available
water is not potable, and roughly 90% of WASH facilities have been damaged or destroyed, sharply raising epidemic risk [1017][983].
Massive waste accumulation (estimated at 900,000 tonnes from October 2023 to December 2025), the destruction or incapacitation of
more than 100 waste-collection machines, and restricted crossings have driven rodent and vector outbreaks, prompting Gaza
human-rights actors to call for urgent crossing openings, pest control inputs, and WHO technical support [980][1003].
Systematic targeting of journalists and repeated attacks on health services undermine independent reporting, accountability, and
protection of civilians, compounding obstacles to rule-of-law, humanitarian access, and human-rights compliance [1039][984]. Israeli
withholding of Palestinian tax revenues for nearly a year has further weakened Palestinian institutional capacity and fiscal space for
services, recovery, and reconstruction [1027][1040]. Settlement expansion in the West Bank — including the approval of 34 new
settlements and allocation of significant infrastructure funding — has eroded Palestinian Authority authority and closed political
avenues for a negotiated settlement [986][1048].
Policy reforms urgently needed include: the establishment of clear conditions, independent oversight mechanisms, and rights-based
safeguards for reconstruction — including Palestinian-led and transparent governance structures — to prevent profit-driven or
exclusionary rebuilding processes [967][992][975]; repeal of the death-penalty law applicable to Palestinians in military courts, and
restoration of fair-trial guarantees for Palestinian detainees [1011][1047][1035]; a halt to settlement expansion incompatible with the
Fourth Geneva Convention; restoration of full clearance revenue transfers to Palestinian authorities; and meaningful international
enforcement mechanisms to ensure compliance with UNSC Resolution 2803 and applicable IHL obligations [1019][1018].
18
Sectoral Analysis
Food Security and Livelihoods
Access to Food and Market Functionality
Gaza
As of late April 2026, Gaza's local food system is effectively collapsed: almost all farmland is inaccessible or destroyed and domestic
food production has stopped, leaving the population highly dependent on imported aid and supplies [1099][1089]. Food and essential
inputs are intermittently available because crossings and maritime routes remain tightly controlled and markets operate under a
policy of rotating/restricted imports, producing chronic instability in stock levels and supplies [1089]. Only about 39% of the 600 agreed
daily truck deliveries have been entering, and fuel shipments meet roughly 14.9% of requirements, undermining bakeries, water,
electricity and service restoration [1089]. WFP-supported bakery and distribution operations depend on a steady flow of at least ~30
aid lorries per day, but deliveries are frequently delayed or blocked and WFP warned support to bakeries may be reduced in the weeks
ahead [1093]. Cuts to flour and diesel have reduced bakery output from ~300 to ~200 tonnes per day — a roughly 50% shortfall —
threatening basic bread access [1093]. The conflict-driven disruption to energy and transport has sharply reduced market
functionality, with widespread generator failures, fuel shortages and transport paralysis interrupting bakery operations, cold chains
and food transport [1147]. Affordability has deteriorated further as private water costs rose by up to ~500%, pushing basic food and
utility costs beyond many households' purchasing power [1103][1085]. Malnutrition and acute food insecurity remain severe:
IPC-confirmed famine conditions occurred in parts of Gaza in 2025, agencies report very high child malnutrition with young children
consuming only 1–2 food groups, and tens of thousands are at acute risk [1073][1099]. In the West Bank, intensified operations and
movement restrictions continue to disrupt market access and livelihoods, contributing to widespread job losses and deepening food
access problems across the occupied Palestinian territory [1092][1074].
Coping Mechanisms
General
Households in Gaza and the West Bank are resorting to severe food-consumption coping and heavy reliance on external food
assistance as local food systems and livelihoods collapse [1099][1074]. Many people have turned to informal, unstable and hazardous
work — including debris recycling — while women and children are bearing increased care and livelihood burdens [1074]. Severe WASH
breakdowns have driven households to desperate water coping strategies such as collecting air-conditioning condensate, re-using
washing water, prioritizing water for infants, and queuing for tanker deliveries, exposing children to safety risks during collection
[1126][1130]. Massive displacement, widespread destruction of homes and blocked crossings have depleted household coping
capacities amid an estimated ~84% contraction in Gaza's economy and widespread housing and infrastructure loss, increasing
reliance on aid for basic needs [1094][1074].
Livelihood Disruption
General
According to Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics (PCBS) data released on 30 April 2026, Gaza's unemployment was 68% in 2025
and youth (15–29) NEET rose to 74%, while West Bank unemployment reached 28% in Q4 2025 (up from 13% pre-war); overall
employment fell from 868,000 to 736,000 (a loss of ~132,000 jobs) and Palestinians working inside Israel declined from 172,000 to 51,000
by Q4 2025 [1095]. The General Federation of Trade Unions and related union statements reported roughly 550,000 workers without
income and claimed unemployment of about 85% in Gaza and 38% in the West Bank, noting that over 250,000 workers were denied
access to workplaces inside Israel since October 2023 [1113][1129]. The war, blockade and related measures have driven near-total
collapse of Gaza's productive sectors — with large shares of factories, industrial facilities, small businesses and agricultural land
destroyed or damaged, supply chains disrupted, and direct reconstruction needs reaching tens of billions of dollars — forcing many
into informal, low-paid activities such as debris recycling [1095][1089][1124][1074]. Movement restrictions, repeated crossing closures
and severe limits on fuel and aid deliveries have blocked raw materials and market access, constrained job opportunities and pushed
people into hazardous attempts to reach work, with dozens of workers killed and thousands arrested since October 2023 [1089][1107].
Trade unions and monitoring bodies report widespread wage erosion and lack of social protection — about 90% of workers lack social
protection, many public salaries are paid partially or late, and a large share of private-sector workers lack formal contracts or receive
below-minimum wages — eroding household purchasing power and increasing reliance on credit and aid [1113][1077].
Impact on Agricultural Activities and Production
Gaza
Mercy Corps reported that 96% of Gaza's agricultural land was either destroyed or inaccessible, with greenhouses, wells and irrigation
systems damaged and soils contaminated by heavy metals and explosive remnants, leaving local food production at a standstill
[1099]. A Palestinian Centre for Political Studies assessment estimated more than 86% of Gaza's agricultural land was affected,
described a near-total collapse of water and livestock systems, and warned that available funding covers less than 10% of urgent
rehabilitation needs while comprehensive reconstruction costs exceed $4.2 billion [1102]. Physical damage in Gaza is estimated at
about $35.2 billion, and over 1.9 million people have been displaced, further undermining agricultural livelihoods and labour availability
[1094]. Large-scale displacement and loss of access to land — including eastern areas designated as military zones — have paralyzed
domestic agricultural production and increased dependence on external assistance [1089][1068]. 
West Bank
19
In the West Bank, the Ministry of Agriculture launched the "Living Palestine/Lift-Palestine" programme (July 2025–June 2029) with a 7.5
million shekel budget to rehabilitate agricultural infrastructure, improve water management and irrigation, and support
climate-resilient production in Jenin, Salfit, Tubas and Hebron, implemented with We Effect, PHG, LRC, Development Work Centre and
ARIJ [1108][1104].
Food and Livelihood Needs and Current Response
Gaza
Humanitarian food assistance in Gaza remains heavily dependent on external deliveries and constrained by access and logistics.
Humanitarian actors continue in-kind distributions and hot-meal provision; for example, a KSrelief convoy delivered 1,210 food baskets
reaching about 7,260 people and its central kitchen provided 25,000 meals in central and southern Gaza [1132]. The Global Report on
Food Crises and sector analyses confirm famine in parts of Gaza in 2025 and ongoing acute child malnutrition, sustaining urgent
nutrition needs [1073][1099]. On recovery and coordination, the Palestinian Ministry of Agriculture has signed a five-year framework
with UNOPS to support infrastructure recovery, spatial planning and capacity building to coordinate reconstruction and donor
engagement [1141]. Key gaps remain: severe access restrictions, critical fuel shortfalls, large-scale agricultural destruction and acute
funding deficits — available funding covers under 10% of urgent agricultural reconstruction needs — limit the reach and effectiveness
of cash, in-kind and livelihood support and prolong dependence on emergency food distributions [1089][1102][1130]. The sharp
economic contraction and rising poverty have cut household purchasing power and driven dependence on humanitarian assistance,
prompting livelihood recovery interventions such as the Lift-Palestine agricultural programme (July 2025–June 2029, 7.5 million NIS) to
support farmer resilience and restore income sources [1138][1108].
Education
Learning Environment and Facility Conditions
Gaza
Almost all schools in Gaza have been damaged or destroyed, with UN-linked reporting confirming nine out of ten school buildings
damaged or destroyed, 792 teachers killed, and 18,639 students killed [1166][1176]. A joint UN/EU/World Bank assessment estimated
recovery and reconstruction needs at US$71.4 billion [1176]. Schools across the occupied West Bank have also been directly targeted or
disrupted — including demolition of classrooms, attacks on students, and incidents where checkpoints blocked teachers from
reaching schools — prompting temporary suspensions of classes [1166]. Many schools are being used as shelters where sanitation
systems and septic tanks are failing, causing sewage leaks that further degrade learning spaces [1195]. Humanitarian actors, including
Save the Children, are running child-friendly spaces, psychosocial support, and informal learning activities to partially replace formal
schooling while recovery and safe access remain limited [1168]. The Palestinian Ministry of Public Works and Housing signed a
memorandum of understanding with UNOPS to support early recovery and reconstruction of public buildings and transitional shelter
solutions, a framework that includes rebuilding schools and improving supply chains for construction materials [1185].
Access to Education and Barriers
Gaza
More than 600,000 school-age children in Gaza are approaching the end of a third year without formal in-person education [1166].
Settler violence and Israeli military actions have directly targeted schools and learning routes in the West Bank: settlers razed
classrooms, toilets, and playgrounds in villages such as Hammamat al-Maleh, placed razor-wire across the road to the Umm al-Khair
school on 13 April blocking students, and shots fired near Mughayyir boys' secondary school on 21 April prompted at least a week of
suspended classes as families and teachers assessed safety [1166]. Checkpoints and roadblocks regularly impede teachers'
movement to schools, and broader access restrictions and displacement orders — covering more than 80% of Gaza and preventing
access to approximately 58% of its territory — constrain returns to schools and humanitarian education support [1196]. Over 80% of
more than 1,600 displacement sites reported visible rodents or pests as of mid-April, affecting an estimated 1.4 million people including
roughly 680,000 children, worsening health risks that further impede learning and attendance [1168]. The extensive destruction of
education and WASH infrastructure, combined with overcrowded shelters and pest infestations, is increasing disease risk and
preventing children from enrolling, attending, or safely learning in person [1176][1189][1168].
Education Needs and Current Response
Gaza
Immediate education needs include rehabilitation of damaged schools, establishment of temporary learning spaces and mobile play
and learning centres, provision of learning materials and trained teachers, expanded psychosocial support, and reliable WASH in
learning environments [1167][1187]. Humanitarian actors have scaled emergency education responses: the Youm Jadeed audio
programme reached over 160,000 children via radio, simple audio files, and group listening sessions, and has been integrated into
temporary learning spaces, while mobile play and child-friendly spaces and psychosocial services are being provided by partners
including the Teacher Creativity Center and Save the Children [1167][1168]. On 27 April 2026, the Palestinian Ministry of Public Works and
Housing and UNOPS signed a five-year Memorandum of Understanding to support early recovery and reconstruction, including school
rebuilding, transitional shelter solutions, technical advisory support, and donor mobilisation [1207][1185]. Major gaps remain: attacks on
schools and teachers have reduced teaching capacity and interrupted attendance, donor-funded and co-funded schools have been
demolished, and restrictions on the entry of materials coupled with insufficient funding continue to impede rehabilitation and safe
reopening of education facilities [1166][1227][1172].
20
These constraints increase the urgency for large-scale, coordinated funding and unimpeded access for repair materials, WASH
supplies, learning materials, and specialist education and psychosocial teams to restore safe, inclusive, and continuous learning for
Palestinian children [1196][1224].
Health
Availability and Access to Healthcare Services
Gaza
Gaza's health system remains severely degraded, with no hospital fully operational and only about half partially functioning. UN/OCHA
reported that only 296 of 683 health service points were functioning and just 23 fully operational as of late April 2026 [1307][1258]. More
than 18,500 patients require medical evacuation outside the Strip, including around 4,000 children [1311][1243]. Hospitals face critical
shortages of essential medicines and oxygen — official Gaza data indicate 59% of essential medicines and 37% of medical
consumables at zero stock — as well as severe fuel and spare-parts deficits that leave facilities dependent on generators at high risk
of failure, disrupting intensive care, neonatal incubators, dialysis and surgical capacity [1243][1302][1297][1274][1257]. Medical
evacuations continue but remain constrained; on 27 April 2026, the Palestine Red Crescent Society, in coordination with WHO,
facilitated the evacuation of 189 people (81 patients and 108 companions) via Karm Abu Salem [1303].
Shortages of fetal-monitoring devices, labour-inducing medications, antibiotics and staff have increased reliance on caesarean
deliveries and post-operative infection risks, while malnutrition, anaemia and rising skin, respiratory and gastrointestinal illnesses are
being reported among children and pregnant or breastfeeding women [1293][1260][1257]. Detention and targeting of health workers —
including the detention of senior clinicians and a group of at least 14 doctors cited in a Physicians for Human Rights–Israel petition —
have reduced workforce capacity and hindered efforts to rehabilitate healthcare and restore services [1244][1305][1277][1309].
Movement restrictions, drastically reduced aid volumes and constrained fuel deliveries continue to block infrastructure repair and
sustained service restoration [1243][1292]. Rights groups and health authorities warn of elevated epidemic risk from accumulated
waste, rodents and lack of pest control, and call for urgent entry of medicines, WASH supplies and technical support to prevent
outbreaks such as leptospirosis or cholera [1281][1294][1274].
Disease Outbreaks
Gaza
Between late April and early May 2026, UN agencies and NGOs warned of sharply escalating infectious-disease risks in Gaza, driven by
collapsed water and sanitation systems, overcrowded displacement sites and reduced healthcare capacity [1259][1247]. Key
indicators include:
- Over 80% of more than 1,600 displacement sites assessed in mid-April reported visible rodents or pests [1259].
- Skin infections were reported in nearly two-thirds of assessed sites, lice in over 65% and bedbugs in more than half [1259].
- Save the Children estimated approximately 1.4 million people were living in overcrowded displacement sites at high risk of
pest-related disease transmission [1259].
- WHO and health authorities reported more than 17,000 rodent- and parasite-related injuries since the start of 2026 [1264], with
separate WHO reporting indicating roughly 111,500 cases of disease or infestation due to external parasites this year [1254].
- MSF documented that skin diseases made up nearly 18% of its primary-care consultations in 2025 and that nearly 25% of people
surveyed between May–August 2025 had experienced gastrointestinal illness in the prior month [1253][1257].
- Approximately 60% of families did not receive their daily clean-water needs, worsening exposure to waterborne disease [1287].
Nearly 90% of Gaza's water and sanitation infrastructure has been damaged or destroyed, and one in five MSF water distributions ran
dry between May–November 2025 [1257][1267]. Humanitarian water operations at some points were suspended following security
incidents that killed aid workers, including an NGO worker at a Gaza water well and two UNICEF-contracted drivers, further constraining
delivery [1288].
The Gaza Centre for Human Rights and health actors have urged urgent pest-control measures, enhanced disease surveillance and
targeted interventions — including vaccines and treatments — to address risks from leptospirosis, cholera, scabies and typhoid [1281].
Humanitarians warn that unless WASH infrastructure, pest control and medical supply lines are restored, conditions in displacement
sites pose a high and imminent risk of outbreaks [1253][1281].
Health System Challenges
Gaza
Gaza's health system is operating at near-collapse. Only 296 of 683 health service points were functioning as of late April 2026, with
just 23 fully operational [1307][1258]. Hospitals depend on generators amid critical fuel and spare-parts shortages, which have
disrupted intensive care, neonatal incubators and dialysis and forced postponement of many surgeries [1302][1243][1297]. Official
Gaza data report 59% of essential medicines and 37% of medical consumables at zero stock, and WHO and partners have urgently
called for expedited entry of medicines, oxygen supplies and spare parts [1243][1274][1257].
WASH-system collapse has further amplified health risks: nearly 90% of water and sanitation infrastructure has been damaged or
destroyed, driving infectious-disease risk and forcing reliance on humanitarian water provision [1278][1267][1257].
21
Movement restrictions, drastically reduced aid volumes and constrained fuel deliveries continue to block infrastructure repair and
sustained service restoration [1243][1292].
Detention and targeting of health workers have reduced workforce capacity and impeded recovery efforts [1244][1277][1309].
Humanitarian actors remain essential but overstretched, delivering primary and surgical care through field hospitals and mobile
teams while systemic capacity gaps persist [1248]. Maternal and surgical care quality is deteriorating, with shortages of
fetal-monitoring devices, labour-inducing drugs, antibiotics and laboratory capacity driving up emergency caesarean rates and
post-operative infection risks [1293].
Mental Health and Psychosocial Support (MHPSS)
Gaza
MSF mental-health teams documented high levels of psychological distress among displaced people in Gaza, including widespread
distress linked to lack of water, sanitation and overcrowding, with instances of suicidal ideation reported [1253]. Save the Children
reported providing psychosocial support services and child-friendly spaces for children in Gaza alongside health, nutrition and WASH
assistance as of 1 May 2026 [1259]. The Palestinian Ministry of Social Development highlighted a sharp rise in orphans — estimated at
approximately 64,616 — and called for large-scale psychosocial support programmes to help children cope with trauma and
displacement as of 2 May 2026 [1318].
The ability to deliver integrated MHPSS is severely constrained by health-facility functionality, with only 296 of 683 health service points
functioning and just 23 fully operational, limiting clinics' and hospitals' capacity to provide such services [1307]. WASH collapse and
access restrictions further limit the scale and integration of MHPSS into the broader humanitarian response [1307][1267][1274]. The
Gaza Centre for Human Rights has called on WHO and UN agencies to dispatch urgent specialized technical teams and to provide
vaccines, medicines and other support to manage compounding health and psychosocial risks, a demand echoed by humanitarian
actors calling for scaled, unfettered access [1281].
Health Needs and Current Response
Gaza
Health needs are concentrated in Gaza, where fuel shortages and WASH system degradation have driven increased malnutrition,
diarrhoeal and skin diseases, and rodent- and parasite-related injuries, creating high risk of epidemic outbreaks and strained referral
pathways [1247][1257][1260][1254][1264]. WHO and UN agencies have called for urgent entry of medicines and supplies to restore
services and are monitoring attacks on healthcare, displacement patterns and service functionality to target trauma care,
noncommunicable disease continuity and WASH/infection prevention and control interventions [1274][1247][1307].
International Medical Corps (IMC), as of 27 April 2026, reported the following response figures across 31 mobile and satellite units that
reached 115 shelters:
- 11,317 consultations delivered since the escalation began
- Acute medications provided to 6,119 people; chronic treatments to 1,332 people
- 702 referrals for advanced care; 227 children received routine vaccinations
- 2,115 health-awareness sessions held; 760 hygiene kits distributed
- 650 children and pregnant or breastfeeding women screened for nutrition (324 received supplementation)
- 583 people reached with psychological first aid and non-specialized psychosocial support [1248][1296]
UNRWA reported 20 of 26 primary health centres in Lebanon operational as of 28 April, with continued mobile-clinic activity and
partner coordination supporting displaced populations in shelters [1279][1280]. MSF remained a major water and health responder in
Gaza, distributing over 5.3 million litres of water per day in March 2026 (meeting minimum needs for approximately 407,000 people),
while warning that one-third of requests to import critical water and sanitation equipment had been rejected or left unanswered
[1267][1257][1278][1276].
Key service coverage gaps include severely reduced facility functionality, major shortages of medicines and oxygen, critical fuel and
spare-part shortfalls threatening generators and ambulances, and restricted entry of water and sanitation equipment that
undermines disease prevention and service restoration [1307][1274][1297][1257]. Coordination is ongoing between UN agencies, IMC,
UNRWA, national health authorities and humanitarian partners for mobile clinics, referrals and MHPSS integration, but agencies warn of
funding and access shortfalls that limit scale-up and reconstruction [1248][1279][1247][1257][1281].
Nutrition
Availability and Access to Nutrition Services
Gaza
As of 27 April, International Medical Corps reported that 31 mobile primary care units had covered 115 shelters, delivering 11,317
consultations across those shelters, screening 650 children under five and pregnant or breastfeeding women, and providing
supplements and referrals to 324 of those individuals [1332]. Mobile and fixed nutrition services are operational but remain far short of
needs due to restricted access, funding cuts, and blocked or limited entry of essential food, therapeutic, and WASH supplies
[1338][1345][1341].
22
Malnutrition caseloads are severe: clinics in Gaza reported receiving 75 children in a single working day, approximately half of recent
cases were moderate malnutrition, and high rates of anaemia have been documented among children and pregnant women
alongside critical shortages of protein and milk [1324][1331][1336]. The Global Report on Food Crises and related UN analyses confirm
that famine conditions were declared in parts of Gaza and that acute malnutrition levels remain critical [1341][1330].
Health-system constraints — including staff and medicine shortages, damaged facilities, and limited fuel and operational supplies —
are limiting sustained treatment and maternal and child nutrition services [1336][1366][1337]. MSF and other agencies report
near-total damage to water and sanitation infrastructure (approximately 90%), frequent rejections or non-responses to requests for
desalination units, pumps, chlorine, and other WASH supplies, and water shortages that undermine safe infant feeding through unsafe
formula preparation and increase diarrhoeal disease and malnutrition risk [1338][1339][1326]. Widespread displacement, overcrowded
shelters, sewage leaks, and rodent and pest outbreaks are further driving increases in diarrhoea, skin disease, and other infections that
compound malnutrition risk among infants and young children [1324][1331][1349]. Urgent scale-up of therapeutic foods, infant milk and
formula, micronutrients, WASH inputs, and staffing is required to adequately address the nutrition crisis [1338][1345][1341].
Nutrition Needs and Current Response
Gaza
The nutrition situation in Gaza continues to deteriorate. The IPC and other global food analyses confirmed famine conditions in parts of
Gaza and reported that up to 90% of children under two consume no more than two food groups, with tens of thousands of children at
acute risk of severe malnutrition or death [1348][1341]. Over 80% of assessed displacement sites had visible rodents or pests and high
rates of skin and diarrhoeal conditions as of mid-April, according to UN OCHA and Save the Children, increasing vulnerability among
children and undermining recovery from malnutrition [1349].
Food availability and market support are strained: WFP-supported bakery and fuel assistance has been curtailed, reducing bakery
output from approximately 300 to 200 tonnes per day and putting bread access at further risk if funding or supplies are cut [1345]. MSF
and other actors warn that the lack of clean water and the inability to safely prepare infant formula — compounded by the repeated
rejection or non-response to roughly one-third of requests for critical WASH supplies — are directly undermining infant and young child
feeding and heightening malnutrition risks [1326][1338][1355].
Key gaps constraining the nutrition response include blocked or delayed entry of critical supplies such as desalination units, pumps,
chlorine, and therapeutic foods; shortages of infant milk, formula, and animal-source proteins; cuts or imminent reductions in
food-assistance funding; and operational constraints that limit the scale-up of therapeutic feeding and community nutrition services
[1338][1355][1324][1331][1345][1341].
WASH
Availability of Water Sources
Gaza
Gaza's water and sanitation systems have been largely destroyed or rendered inoperable, with nearly 90% of infrastructure — including
desalination plants, boreholes, pipelines, and sewage systems — damaged or destroyed, per MSF citing UN/EU/World Bank data
[1381][1396][1397]. Repeat attacks on distribution assets, long-standing restrictions on fuel, generators, spare parts, and imports have
severely degraded production and distribution capacity and exposed civilians and aid workers to direct harm [1381][1382].
UNICEF reported average daily supply across Gaza of about 7 litres of drinking water and 16 litres of domestic water, with many people
lacking even 6 litres of clean drinking water [1395]. The Deir al-Balah desalination plant, serving up to approximately 400,000 people,
was reduced to around 20% capacity after an airstrike damaged its power line while spare parts and fuel were delayed [1395].
Municipal tanker capacity is critically reduced: Gaza reportedly needs approximately 100 water trucks but only around 15 remain, and
in some localities trucks arrive only weekly or during short approximately two-hour windows, forcing long queues and extended
collection times [1395][1382].
In March 2026, MSF produced and distributed about 5.3 million litres of water per day, meeting minimum needs for roughly 407,000
people — approximately one-fifth of the Strip — leaving large gaps in overall coverage [1382][1381]. UN partners reported that roughly
60% of families did not receive their daily clean water needs from trucking and other temporary measures [1380]. Water prices rose by
up to 500% between October 2023 and January 2026, placing purchased water beyond the reach of most households [1374][1382].
Humanitarian operations have faced repeated access denials and supply rejections. MSF reports that one in five of its distributions ran
dry between May and November 2025, and that approximately one-third of its requests to import desalination units, pumps, tanks, and
treatment chemicals have been rejected or left unanswered since October 2023, with further denials recorded through the dedicated
approval system since 1 January 2026 [1381][1382][1374].
Access to Sanitation Facilities and Hygiene Practices
Gaza
Sanitation systems in Gaza have effectively collapsed. Only 16 of Gaza's 78 sewage pumping stations were operational according to
the coastal municipalities water authority, worsening raw sewage discharge and contamination risks [1401]. Displaced families are
forced to dig makeshift latrines in tents or share overcrowded, rapidly filling facilities often sited close to boreholes, contaminating
groundwater and overflowing during heavy rain [1374][1381][1382]. Displaced people live with little privacy and undignified sanitation
arrangements, a condition MSF links to increased distress among women, the elderly, and people with disabilities [1374].
23
Hygiene items — soap, disinfectant, diapers, and menstrual products — are scarce or prohibitively expensive, further undermining
households' ability to maintain personal and household hygiene [1374][1382]. People routinely travel 15–60 minutes to reach water
trucks, queue, reuse old containers, and prioritise drinking over washing, undermining handwashing and other hygiene practices
[1382].
Health impacts documented by MSF include high levels of diarrhoeal disease — nearly 25% of people reported gastrointestinal illness
in May–August 2025 — and skin conditions accounting for almost 18% of primary care consultations in 2025, with children, pregnant
women, and other vulnerable groups disproportionately affected [1374][1381][1382]. Movement restrictions, military displacement
orders, and the inability to carry out repairs have further degraded services and disproportionately affected displaced and
marginalised populations in camps and shelters [1381][1382][1428].
Waste Management and Vector-Borne Disease Risks
Gaza
Gaza's waste management system has effectively collapsed. An estimated 900,000 tonnes of waste accumulated between October
2023 and December 2025, more than 100 waste collection machines were destroyed, and remaining equipment lacks maintenance,
oil, and fuel [1414][1410]. Halted collection and blocked access to official dumps have left large rubbish piles adjacent to displacement
sites, creating ideal breeding grounds for rodents, flies, mosquitoes, and fleas and heightening epidemic risk [1414][1374]. Solid waste
collection has halted in many areas, producing large accumulations in living areas and fuelling widespread rodent and pest
infestations [1374][1399][1409].
UN OCHA assessments in mid-April found rodents or pests frequently visible in over 80% of more than 1,600 displacement sites
assessed, affecting roughly 1.4–1.45 million people living in overcrowded sites [1409][1398]. The World Health Organization and local
health authorities reported approximately 17,000 direct rodent- and parasite-related injuries and around 111,500 cases of infestation or
disease due to external parasites this year, while skin infections or rashes were present in nearly two-thirds of displacement sites, lice
in over 65%, and bedbugs in more than half [1419][1411][1398][1409].
Critical vector-control items are largely unavailable due to restrictions and cost: local actors and rights groups report that pesticides
and rodenticides have been denied entry under dual-use pretexts, even as some shipments — including nearly 1,000 rat traps and
approximately 10 tonnes of pesticides — were later facilitated for humanitarian use [1414][1398]. Humanitarian actors warn that
massive waste accumulation, collapsed sanitation, depleted vector control capacity, and dense displacement are driving outbreaks
of scabies, diarrhoeal, and skin diseases and could precipitate larger epidemics without urgent intervention [1374][1381][1409]. Gaza
civil society and humanitarian agencies have called for the immediate opening of crossings, rapid entry of heavy equipment,
pesticides, rodent poisons, fuel, and specialised WHO/UN technical teams, along with urgent donor funding to support municipal waste
operations and large-scale pest control and sanitation responses [1414][1396][1409].
Main WASH Needs and Humanitarian Response
Gaza
The WASH situation in Gaza reflects a near-total breakdown of infrastructure and services. Palestinians face acute shortages of clean
water, collapsed sanitation systems, and severe shortages of hygiene items, forcing reliance on unsafe or saline sources and
makeshift latrines in displacement sites [1374][1382]. The scale of infrastructure destruction — with nearly 90% of water and sanitation
assets damaged or destroyed — has sharply reduced local production and treatment capacity, and restoration remains blocked by
access constraints, fuel and electricity shortages, equipment import denials, insecurity for repair crews, and damaged assets
[1382][1396][1374].
The humanitarian WASH response has relied primarily on large-scale water production and trucking by MSF and municipal actors,
alongside ad hoc hygiene promotion. In March 2026, MSF produced or distributed approximately 5.3 million litres of drinking water per
day, covering the minimum needs of roughly 407,000 people — about one in five of Gaza's population [1382][1396]. However, critical
inputs for recovery — desalination units, pumps, chlorine, tanks, latrines, generators, and fuel — have been repeatedly rejected or left
unanswered, with MSF reporting approximately one-third of requests denied or unanswered since October 2023 and further denials
since January 2026 [1381][1374][1395]. Israeli-imposed movement and displacement orders, as well as repeated incidents of water
trucks or wells being shot at, have further constrained operations and repairs [1381][1374][1395].
Key unmet needs include the restoration of water supply infrastructure, rehabilitation of sanitation systems, and scaled-up hygiene
promotion. Approximately one-third of MSF's requests to import WASH supplies — including desalination units, pumps, chlorine, tanks,
and latrines — have been denied or left unanswered since October 2023 [1381][1382][1428]. The distribution of hygiene kits and water
purification efforts remain insufficient, as emergency interventions cover only a fraction of the population and structural barriers
prevent meaningful scale-up of the WASH response [1382][1374].
Shelter and Non-Food Items (NFI)
Damage to Housing and Shelter Needs
General
The joint UN–EU–World Bank Rapid Damage and Needs Assessment documents massive housing destruction and displacement,
estimating total recovery and reconstruction needs at approximately US$71.4 billion, including ~US$26.3 billion required during the first
18 months for basic services and critical infrastructure [1431][1430][1458][1433]. Key figures include:
24
- More than 371,000 housing units destroyed or damaged; approximately 1.9 million people displaced; over 60% of the population
homeless [1431][1430][1458][1433].
- Only ~2,000 housing units have been delivered (under 1% of assessed need) [1434][1439].
- An estimated 61 million tonnes of rubble with less than 1% removed to date; UNDP warned debris clearance at current pace could
take about seven years, and Palestinian civil defence data estimate some 8,000 bodies remain under the rubble [1480][1430].
- Roughly 89% of water and sanitation infrastructure has been damaged or destroyed, driving sewage leakage, contamination,
and heightened disease risk [1445].
UN experts and the assessment highlight disproportionate impacts on women (including widows and female-headed households),
children, older people, and persons with disabilities; the Palestinian Ministry of Social Development reports around 64,616 orphans
following the conflict surge [1431][1458][1477]. Shelters remain overcrowded with widespread rodent and insect infestations, and WHO
has registered large numbers of rodent- and parasitic-related injuries since the start of the year [1434][1439].
Immediate shelter priorities identified by local authorities and partners include provision of durable shelter materials, transitional
housing, and decongestion and sanitation improvements in priority areas such as Khan Younis and Jabalia. UNOPS and the Palestinian
Ministry have signed a memorandum of understanding to support transitional shelter, debris recycling, supply-chain facilitation for
construction materials, and geospatial damage prioritization [1434][1439][1465][1492]. Reconstruction and shelter scale-up are
constrained by restrictions on the entry of durable construction and WASH materials, shortages of fuel and heavy equipment, ongoing
safety risks from unexploded ordnance, slow debris-removal capacity, and unresolved questions about governance and rights-based
oversight of the rebuilding process [1461][1445][1480][1431][1458].
Living Conditions in Camps or Settlements
Gaza
Some 90% of Gazans have been forcibly displaced at least once, concentrating large numbers in tents and temporary sites under
severe strain [1432][1440]. UN and partner teams visiting displacement sites found families sheltering in damaged buildings and tents
with little or no access to clean water and virtually no sanitation services; OCHA identified sites with around 600 families living in "harsh
conditions" in eastern Gaza city [1440][1461]. Living spaces are highly overcrowded, with makeshift latrines, shared facilities, and limited
privacy, increasing protection risks for women, children, and persons with disabilities [1445][1431][1434].
Sewage-system destruction, halted waste collection, and accumulating rubbish have fuelled widespread rodent and pest infestations
and increased disease risks, with WHO reporting more than 17,000 rodent- and parasite-related injuries since the start of the year and
Save the Children warning that two in three displaced children are at risk of infection in these conditions [1434][1438][1446]. UNDP and
local rights groups report massive waste accumulation (approximately 900,000 tonnes from October 2023 to December 2025) and
damaged waste-collection equipment, compounding public-health hazards in and around displacement camps [1463]. These
conditions have contributed to mounting malnutrition and disease burdens noted by medical teams, with malnutrition clinics seeing
large daily caseloads and high anaemia rates [1445][1431][1434].
Water and WASH services are severely constrained: MSF reported producing and distributing over 5.3 million litres (approximately 1.4
million gallons) per day in March 2026—meeting minimum needs for about 407,000 people—yet agencies report that roughly one third
of requests to import critical WASH supplies have been rejected or unanswered, and MSF reports its requests through the dedicated
approval system since 1 January 2026 were denied [1441][1469][1435][1457][1445]. MSF and others have also documented incidents of
water trucks, wells, and water-service personnel being struck or killed, further disrupting access [1435][1476][1486]. Humanitarian
actors report intermittent distributions of hygiene kits and mobile health teams reaching shelters (e.g., 760 hygiene kits distributed and
mobile teams covering shelters as of 27 April), but access constraints and ongoing insecurity continue to limit scale-up of lifesaving
WASH, shelter, and disease-prevention interventions [1467][1440].
NFI and Shelter Needs and Current Response
General
Aid agencies report that durable shelter materials are being blocked at crossings, restricting deliveries to tarpaulins, blankets, and
sheets and preventing construction of more resilient shelters [1461]. Persistent access and logistics constraints at crossings—including
substantially reduced truck flows—plus restrictions on materials and fuel remain the main bottlenecks limiting NFI and shelter
distribution, and prolonging overcrowding, waste accumulation, rodent infestation, and associated health risks [1432][1434][1453].
The Palestinian Ministry of Public Works and Housing, working with UN partners including UNDP, is mobilizing to expand tented shelters
in Khan Younis, Jabalia, and other priority areas [1434][1439]. To coordinate recovery and scale up transitional solutions, the Palestinian
Ministry and UNOPS signed a memorandum of understanding covering early recovery, transitional shelter solutions, supply-chain
facilitation for construction materials, and geospatial damage prioritization [1465][1492]. Despite these efforts, the response remains
critically underfunded and insufficient relative to the scale of need, with funding limitations and logistical challenges continuing to
impede delivery to affected populations [1432][1434][1453].
25
Protection
Impact on civilians
General
Humanitarian actors report widespread civilian harm across Gaza and the occupied West Bank, including high death tolls, mass
displacement, large-scale destruction of water and health infrastructure, attacks on civilian infrastructure and humanitarian
personnel, and severe restrictions on movement and aid [1539][1537][1525][1522]. Key figures and operational impacts include:
- At least 72,073 Palestinians killed and 171,756 injured since 7 October 2023 (figures recorded to 23 February 2026) [1539].
- Approximately 1.9 million people displaced, more than 60% of the population having lost their homes, and an estimated 90% of
Gazans displaced at least once, with most remaining in tents or temporary shelters lacking minimum services [1504][1520].
- Nearly 90% of Gaza's water and sanitation infrastructure damaged or destroyed, with around 60% of families lacking adequate
access to clean water; trucking and emergency distributions are described as temporary, costly and unsustainable
[1537][1539][1522][1551].
- Only 296 of 683 health service points are functioning and just 23 are fully operational, severely constraining medical care [1525].
- 149 verified attacks on the health sector since the escalation began, resulting in 100 deaths and 233 injuries among health
personnel and patients [1522].
- Humanitarian staff and NGO workers have been killed or injured during water and aid operations: one NGO worker was killed and
four injured at a Gaza City water well, and UNICEF-contracted drivers were killed at a filling point, causing suspension of
operations at Al Mansoura water filling point [1522][1551][1527].
- Only 41,714 of 110,400 trucks envisaged under the ceasefire entered Gaza over six months (an average of 227 trucks/day versus
600 planned), with repeated ceasefire violations and new displacement orders continuing to limit movement and return [1530].
- Explosive ordnance contamination continues to endanger civilians and responders, with UNMAS recording over 1,200 people killed
or injured by explosive ordnance since October 2023 [1510].
West Bank
Operations in the West Bank — including large-scale searches around Qalandiya Camp — have caused injuries, property damage,
temporary displacement and disrupted access to schools, clinics and ambulances, further aggravating civilian protection needs
[1525]. UN experts and rights bodies warn that sexual and gender-based violence is being used as a tool of intimidation and forcible
displacement, increasing protection risks for women, children and detainees across the occupied Palestinian territory [1497][1501].
Factors Driving protection risks
General
The conflict remains characterised by repeated hostilities and a fragile ceasefire: more than 2,400 Israeli violations were recorded until
mid-April, resulting in 784 Palestinians killed and over 2,200 injured since the truce began [1499]. Remote airstrikes and the use of
explosive weapons between 28 February and 31 March 2026 damaged civilian infrastructure across the region, disrupting essential
services and humanitarian access [1536][1579]. Unexploded ordnance and explosive remnants of war pose a persistent threat, with UN
estimates of over 70,000 UXO items hindering returns and recovery [1510][1544].
United Nations experts warned that sexual and gender-based violence is being used systematically as a tool of control and
contributes to forced displacement, with incidents reported in detention, at checkpoints and during raids, and with accountability
largely absent [1497][1501]. Large-scale arbitrary arrests and detention have undermined protection and social structures, with
thousands of arrests reported since October 2023 and around 1,800 children detained during the conflict period [1524][1523].
Severe economic deprivation and restrictions on movement are driving exploitation and displacement: as of 30 April 2026, the
Palestinian economy had contracted by roughly 24%, the Gaza economy collapsed by about 84%, and unemployment reached
around 46% overall (78% in Gaza and 28% in the West Bank), leaving over 650,000 people unemployed [1550]. Trade unions and labour
bodies report some 550,000 workers without income, mass denial of access to work — including roughly 250,000 formerly employed in
1948 areas — and widespread cases of workers killed or arrested, exacerbating livelihoods collapse and protection risks [1508][1542].
Targeting of journalists and humanitarians — including widespread arrests of media workers, detention of journalists, and killings of
NGO staff and convoy drivers reported in late April — has reduced documentation capacity and increased risks to civilians and
responders [1575][1559][1522][1506]. Legal and institutional weaknesses, including impunity for alleged violations and recent
legislation criticised by UN treaty bodies for discriminatory application against Palestinians, further limit access to justice and heighten
protection vulnerabilities [1599].
Psychological and mental health impacts
Gaza
Humanitarian actors report high levels of trauma, distress and deteriorating psychosocial wellbeing across Gaza. MSF teams have
observed significant distress including suicidal ideation linked to severe WASH deprivation and provided 89,800 mental health sessions
in Gaza in 2025 [1539][1554]. The Palestinian Ministry of Social Development reported more than 64,000 children are now orphans
(reported 2 May 2026), sharply increasing demand for psychosocial support and prompting calls for large-scale MHPSS programmes
[1529].
26
As of 27 April 2026, International Medical Corps mental health teams had reached 583 people with psychological first aid,
non-specialised support, structured case management and specialised care delivered remotely and in person [1557]. WHO and
partners have begun implementing MHPSS activities for displaced communities while warning that damaged health infrastructure
and medicine shortages are constraining mental health service delivery (WHO situation reporting, 29–30 April 2026) [1578].
Major access and service barriers include attacks on infrastructure and health workers, suspension of key water operations after aid
workers were killed, and restricted crossings — all of which undermine mental wellbeing and limit access to care [1522][1551][1539].
Children are disproportionately affected: reports describe children bearing heavy water-collection responsibilities, rising skin and
diarrhoeal disease linked to WASH breakdown, and thousands of children requiring urgent medical evacuation and specialised mental
health care following severe injuries and displacements [1539][1547].
Protection Needs and Current Response
General
Humanitarian protection needs in Gaza and the West Bank are acute, driven by massive displacement, repeated strikes on populated
areas and critical infrastructure, and severe restrictions on humanitarian access that undermine protective services and shelter
conditions [1520][1522][1541]. Protection-specific services — including case management, referrals, legal aid and dedicated protective
shelters — are severely impeded by access, fuel and supply constraints. Documented evacuations and patient transfers have
occurred (approximately 20 patients evacuated via Kerem Abu Salim), but overall referral and continuity-of-care capacity remains
strained [1522].
Humanitarian actors are maintaining monitoring and a limited response despite these constraints. WHO continues to monitor and
verify attacks on health care and has delivered emergency health supplies to support strained services [1578][1557]. OCHA and UN
agencies have reported strikes disrupting operations and stressed the need to protect civilians and civilian infrastructure under
international humanitarian law [1522][1551]. OHCHR has publicly urged that restrictions be lifted and humanitarian access be enabled,
reiterating the obligations of the occupying power to ensure basic needs and protection [1592]. As of 27 April, International Medical
Corps mobile teams had delivered 11,317 consultations, provided acute medications to 6,119 people and chronic treatments to 1,332,
referred 702 patients, vaccinated 227 children, screened 650 children and pregnant or breastfeeding women (324 received
supplementation), and distributed 760 hygiene kits in shelters and displacement sites [1557].
Overall, monitoring systems — including WHO verification of attacks, OCHA reporting and UN/agency advocacy — are active, but the
effectiveness of the humanitarian protection response is significantly limited by access restrictions, attacks on humanitarian
personnel and infrastructure, and shortages of fuel, water and supplies that prevent safe sheltering, service continuity and scaled case
management [1578][1557][1522][1520][1551].
Child Protection concerns
Gaza
Save the Children reported plagues of rats, mice and insects have swarmed Gaza displacement sites in recent weeks, and OCHA's
mid-April assessments found rodents or pests frequently visible in over 80% of more than 1,600 sites, with skin infections, lice and
bedbugs widespread, leaving roughly 680,000 children (about 47% of Gaza's population) exposed to heightened infection risk [1528].
Medical actors and local clinics report rising child malnutrition and disease, with malnutrition clinics overwhelmed — for example, 75
children seen in one working day — and high rates of anaemia, diarrhoeal and skin infections among children [1543][1540][1539][1528].
The Palestinian Ministry of Social Development reported that more than 64,616 children in Gaza are now orphans, many scattered
across temporary shelters after orphanages were damaged or destroyed [1529]. The Palestine Centre for Prisoners' Studies reported
more than 1,800 arrests of minors since the start of the war, with about 350 children reportedly still in detention and allegations of
ill-treatment, including cases of children born or held in prison [1496][1523][1538].
Education has been severely disrupted: over 600,000 school-age children in Gaza have gone without formal in-person education for
nearly three years, thousands of teachers and students have been killed, and roughly nine out of ten school buildings were damaged
or destroyed [1555]. Explosive ordnance and contamination pose major child protection risks — of the over 1,200 people killed or injured
by explosive ordnance in Gaza since October 2023, nearly half the victims are children, and widespread unexploded ordnance
hampers safe returns and recovery [1510][1544].
Restricted WASH access and dangerous water distributions force families to send children to fetch water, exposing them to loss, injury
and harassment. Humanitarian reporting also documents children engaging in negative coping — such as collecting and selling
debris or entering hazardous areas — to obtain income or resources, further increasing protection risks [1539][1528][1511][1529][1510].
Humanitarian actors provide psychosocial support and child-friendly and mobile play and learning spaces, with audio education
reaching over 160,000 children, but warn that services cannot keep pace with mounting needs [1539][1528][1511][1529].
Violence against women and girls
Gaza
United Nations independent experts have warned that sexual and gender-based violence against Palestinians has become
systematic — reported in detention centres, at checkpoints, during house raids and in interactions with both Israeli forces and settlers
— and is being used to intimidate, displace and fragment communities, while investigations and accountability remain rare
[1501][1497]. Palestinian civil society bodies report systematic patterns of arbitrary detention and torture that include sexual assaults in
custody, with renewed detentions noted in late April 2026, underscoring barriers to redress and elevated protection needs for women
detainees and survivors [1591].
27
The Palestinian Ministry of Women's Affairs stated that Israeli occupation practices are driving "compound economic violence" against
women, citing a sharp economic contraction (GDP down approximately 24%), a Gaza economy collapse (approximately 84%) and a
steep rise in unemployment (about 46% overall; approximately 78% in Gaza, approximately 28% in the West Bank), which undermines
women's livelihoods and protection options (statement, 30 April 2026) [1550]. UN agencies and OCHA report that ongoing hostilities,
damaged infrastructure and constrained humanitarian access are forcing mass displacement into overcrowded shelters and
displacement sites — conditions that are increasing psychological distress and heightening risks of gender-based violence for women
and children (late April–early May 2026) [1522][1551].
Médecins Sans Frontières and other health actors document widespread destruction of sexual and reproductive health and WASH
services, severe shortages of menstrual and hygiene supplies, and impeded access to care — factors that reduce survivors' ability to
obtain medical and psychosocial support and undermine women's dignity and health [1539][1562].
Vulnerable Groups / Special Needs Groups
Unaccompanied and Separated Children
Gaza
The Palestinian Ministry of Social Development reported 64,616 children in Gaza are now orphans, with roughly 55,000 registered since
the war began; many have been displaced into temporary sites after orphanages were destroyed [1665]. More than 1,800 Palestinian
children have been arrested since the war began, with around 350 minors remaining in Israeli prisons — 163 convicted and 90 held
under administrative detention [1616][1621][1637]. Medical evacuations have transferred wounded or ill children abroad, including 81
children who arrived in Jordan in the 26th group and more than 716 children transferred since March of last year under the Jordanian
medical corridor [1678].
Humanitarian assessments report children scattered across overcrowded shelters and informal sites with limited access to basic
services and alternative care arrangements, following widespread damage to orphanage and care infrastructure [1665]. Mobile health
and protection teams are providing psychosocial support, child-friendly spaces, nutrition screening and structured case
management. As of 27 April, International Medical Corps mobile units covered 115 shelters, administered routine vaccinations to 227
children, screened 650 children under five (324 of whom received supplementation), and mental health teams reached 583 people
with psychological first aid and case management [1631].
Displacement-site conditions and environmental hazards — including rodents, pests and sewage — increase disease and malnutrition
risks for children in shelters [1645], and children are exposed to safety risks while fetching water or collecting materials to survive
[1633][1615]. UN experts have also documented targeted sexual harassment, humiliating body searches and sexualized ill-treatment
affecting children in the West Bank [1632][1650].
Pregnant and Lactating Women
Gaza
Obstetric services are under severe strain: caesarean deliveries have risen to about one quarter of births, with delays in presentation,
widespread anaemia, overcrowded wards, shortages of antibiotics and supplies, and an increase in surgical wound infections and
other postpartum risks reported by clinicians and humanitarian actors in April 2026 [1609]. Local clinical teams and health officials
have warned of rising malnutrition and high anaemia rates among pregnant women, with malnutrition clinics overwhelmed — one
clinic received 75 children in a single working day — reflecting severe nutritional gaps and disrupted diets [1620][1619]. WHO has urged
immediate entry of medicines and supplies and supported the establishment of a family health centre in northern Gaza to deliver
maternal and child health services, routine vaccination and referrals where access remains extremely limited [1647].
Médecins Sans Frontières (MSF) documented that pregnant and breastfeeding women are presenting with acute watery diarrhoea
linked to lack of clean water — conditions that worsen maternal malnutrition and can undermine breastfeeding. MSF reported
producing and distributing over 4.7 million litres of water per day by January 2026 and approximately 5.3 million litres per day in March
2026, while needs far exceed supply [1633][1622]. Overcrowded displacement sites plagued by rodents, pests, poor sanitation and
limited WASH services are increasing infection and hygiene-related risks for infants and for pregnant and breastfeeding women,
further exacerbating maternal and newborn health vulnerabilities [1645].
Restrictions on crossings, limited fuel and supply entry, and damage to infrastructure have constrained restoration of maternal
services and health system capacity, with agreed aid flows and fuel deliveries remaining far below needs [1630][1610]. Displacement
orders, large-scale shelter overcrowding and dwindling household resources are amplifying protection risks for women, including
heightened psychosocial distress and increased exposure to gender-based violence in overcrowded collective sites [1639].
Adolescents and Youth
Gaza
Education and protection for children and adolescents in Gaza remain severely disrupted: more than 600,000 school-age children are
approaching the end of a third year without formal in-person education, with the UN reporting 792 teachers and 18,639 students killed
and nine out of ten school buildings damaged or destroyed [1636]. Economic opportunities for young people are negligible: Palestinian
Central Bureau of Statistics data published on 30 April 2026 indicate an unemployment rate of approximately 68% in Gaza, with
roughly 74% of young people out of education, training or employment, underscoring acute youth exclusion from the labour market
[1640].
28
Humanitarian actors report widespread psychosocial needs and are delivering mental health and psychosocial support (MHPSS) and
child-friendly services. Save the Children described ongoing psychosocial support, child-friendly spaces and outreach in Gaza
displacement sites amid acute health risks from pests and waste (reported 1 May 2026), while International Medical Corps' mental
health teams reached 583 people with psychological first aid and non-specialized support as of 27 April 2026, and WHO continues
MHPSS interventions for displaced populations [1645][1631][1630]. Documented youth-focused programming in the reporting period
also includes educational media initiatives — for example, the Youm Jadeed audio education programme reached over 160,000
children — and NGOs including Save the Children report supporting child-friendly spaces and offering some employment support for
young people, though large-scale vocational or employment programmes are not detailed in available sources [1651][1645].
People with Disabilities
Gaza
UN experts and joint assessments note that persons with disabilities in Gaza face major accessibility challenges in shelters and during
reconstruction, and are among the groups most severely affected by the crisis [1617][1629]. Large numbers of conflict-related
casualties and trauma injuries have increased the population of people with disabilities, straining limited rehabilitation and assistive
capacity on the ground and leaving amputees and others with new long-term needs amid persistent shortages and access barriers
[1633]. Access to rehabilitation, medical supplies and services — including WHO calls for immediate entry of medicines, spare parts
and basic physical rehabilitation capacity — remains severely constrained by damage to health systems and restrictions on supplies
[1647][1633][1618].
Water-distribution dynamics and forced displacement create specific safety and mobility risks for people with disabilities, who face
greater difficulty fetching water and increased exposure to intimidation and harm at distribution points [1633]. Degraded WASH
services, lack of hygiene supplies and restricted access to sanitation are further undermining health, dignity and infection prevention
for this group, compounding their vulnerabilities [1618][1633]. The Palestinian Ministry of Social Development approved customs
exemptions to expand benefits for persons with disabilities as part of broader targeting and inclusion efforts in assistance delivery
[1655]. Experts call for inclusive, rights-based reconstruction with explicit safeguards to ensure persons with disabilities are not
excluded from recovery, protection and services as rebuilding begins [1617].
Elderly
Gaza
Displacement and damaged shelter and WASH infrastructure have amplified mobility and hygiene challenges for older people, who
are often unable to use shared or makeshift latrines, face uneven, rubbish-strewn grounds and require constant assistance for basic
tasks [1633][1622][1618]. The near-total destruction of water and sanitation systems — reported at nearly 90% in some assessments —
and the rejection or non-response to many requests for critical WASH supplies have worsened dignity and health risks for older people
[1618][1627].
Health services remain extremely limited: no hospital in Gaza is fully operational, many facilities are partially functioning or out of
service, and shortages of medicines, fuel and spare parts are constraining continuity of care for chronic conditions that are
particularly prevalent among older people [1629][1647][1610]. Humanitarian actors report disruptions to rehabilitation, assistive devices
and chronic-care provision, even as mobile teams and field hospitals continue outreach to displaced populations, leaving persistent
gaps in age-adapted services [1630][1631].
Repeated displacement and loss of community networks have increased social isolation and dependence among older people,
heightening their protection and access vulnerabilities in displacement sites [1617][1676]. Reconstruction and recovery assessments
warn that older persons risk exclusion unless rebuilding and aid processes explicitly incorporate accessibility, age-sensitive services
and social support measures [1617].
Displaced
Gaza
Approximately 1.9 million people have been displaced in Gaza, with more than 371,000 housing units destroyed or damaged and over
60% of the population remaining homeless [1617][1677]. Displaced families are sheltering in overcrowded tents, damaged buildings
and temporary sites that lack sanitation and basic services, with UN teams finding around 600 families in harsh conditions in eastern
Gaza city during late April 2026 [1615][1677]. UN agencies report they are unable to bring in materials needed to build durable shelters
or repair generators, leaving only emergency items such as tarpaulins and blankets able to enter [1677].
Water and sanitation infrastructure has been widely destroyed — nearly 90% damage to WASH systems in Gaza — and about 60% of
families do not receive their daily clean water needs, forcing costly, unsustainable reliance on water trucking [1618][1649]. In March
2026, MSF produced or distributed roughly 5.3 million litres of drinking water per day, covering minimum needs for about 407,000
people, yet shortages meant many distributions ran dry during May–November 2025 [1622][1618]. Health services are severely
degraded: only 296 of 683 health service points were functioning and just 23 were fully operational, while authorities report rising
waterborne and rodent-related illness and more than 17,000 rodent- and parasite-related injuries since the start of the year
[1662][1620]. WHO reported more than 18,500 patients in Gaza require medical evacuation outside the territory, including about 4,000
children [1610].
Livelihoods have collapsed: PCBS reported a 68% unemployment rate in Gaza and a marked fall in West Bank employment between Q3
2023 and Q4 2025, with trade unions estimating some 550,000 workers without income [1640][1638][1644]. The Palestinian Ministry of
Social Development launched a digital registry linking some 350,000 families in Gaza — covering about 90% of the population — to
target emergency cash support, representing an institutional effort to improve assistance delivery [1655].
29
UN experts and rights bodies warn that sexual and gender-based violence is being used as both a driver and consequence of forced
displacement, and humanitarian operations have been directly endangered, with NGO staff killed at a water well and
UNICEF-contracted drivers also killed while operating water distribution points [1650][1632][1639][1649]. The scale of destruction,
contamination by unexploded ordnance, and restrictions on materials and access make safe returns and meaningful reconstruction
infeasible without major changes to access, security and rights-based guarantees — a point underscored by UN experts warning that
reconstruction will fail while the occupation continues [1615][1677][1617].
Minorities
General
UN independent experts warned that reconstruction must address structural discrimination and be Palestinian-led, noting that
housing destruction and displacement have disproportionately affected women (including widows and female-headed households),
persons with disabilities and older people, and calling for inclusive, participatory decision-making and rights-based safeguards in
rebuilding processes [1617]. UN assessments and experts have stressed that recovery must include remedies, reparations and explicit
safeguards to prevent renewed displacement and to correct entrenched patterns of discrimination against Palestinians [1617][1626].
UNOPS has entered a multi-year partnership with the Palestinian Ministry of Public Works and Housing to support Palestinian-led
infrastructure and reconstruction projects, signaling institutional efforts to embed local leadership in recovery planning and
implementation [1708].
Human Rights Watch and the UN Committee on the Elimination of Racial Discrimination (CERD) stated that the Israeli law adopted on
30 March 2026 to apply the death penalty in military courts is discriminatory in practice against Palestinians, undermines due-process
guarantees and should be repealed, with calls for states not to support or enable discriminatory enforcement [1664][1702][1682]. UN
human rights experts and independent investigators have documented sexual and gender-based violence used as a tool of control
that contributes to forced displacement, reporting that investigations are rare and accountability is largely absent [1650][1632].
Key socio-economic indicators cited by the Palestinian Minister of Women's Affairs on 30 April 2026 include:
- GDP contracted by around 24 percent [1690].
- Gaza's economy contracted by about 84 percent [1690].
- Unemployment reached roughly 46 percent overall — approximately 78 percent in Gaza and 28 percent in the West Bank — with
more than 650,000 people unemployed [1690].
30
Governorates
West Bank
Ramallah & Al-Bireh
- In the Ramallah & Al-Bireh governorate, the period between late April and early May 2026 was marked by significant violence,
settler attacks, military raids, and civilian suffering across multiple towns and villages.
- On April 21, a shooter in military fatigues opened fire toward a school in al-Mughayyir village, northeast of Ramallah, killing two
people including a teenager. Israeli forces subsequently closed the village's entrances and attacked mourners at the funeral,
according to the Palestine Red Crescent Society and WAFA. On April 24, a resident of Deir Dibwan, east of Ramallah, died of
wounds sustained in a settler attack, after which Israeli forces arrested approximately 30 residents of the town. The Ramallah and
Al-Bireh Governor briefed British Deputy National Security Adviser Barbara Woodward on these incidents on April 28, during a field
visit to Sinjil and several villages in eastern Ramallah. The Governor specifically cited the killing of student Aws al-Naasan and
citizen Jihad Abu al-Naeem during the al-Mughayyir attack, as well as the death of resident Odeh Awawdeh in Deir Dibwan,
whose infant twin daughters were left without a father. The governor also highlighted the ongoing situation in the towns of Kafr
Malik, Burqa, Deir Jarir, and Umm Safa, which continue to face daily attacks by Israeli forces and settlers. The town of Sinjil itself is
encircled by a fence, its entrances closed, with residents facing severe restrictions on movement. Also on April 28, British Deputy
National Security Adviser Woodward affirmed her country's rejection of colonist attacks and committed to continued follow-up
on these violations.
- On April 30, Israeli forces detained four citizens during raids on al-Mughayyir village and Birzeit town within the Ramallah &
Al-Bireh governorate. Earlier, Israeli forces raided the town of Surda, north of Ramallah, setting up a checkpoint on the main road
and stopping vehicles, and also raided homes in the village of Shuqba in the Ramallah area, detaining about 35 residents who
were reportedly physically assaulted before being released. Israeli forces stormed the town of Birzeit (also referenced as
Perzeit/Birzeit) and raided a number of houses, arresting at least one youth. The Jalazone refugee camp, north of Ramallah, was
stormed by Israeli forces on the evening of May 3, with military forces deploying across several areas of the camp, though no
detentions were reported at that time. The village of Deir Jarir, northeast of Ramallah, was also subject to a house raid as part of
a broader West Bank campaign, and a home was raided in Kafr Malik, east of Ramallah.
- In the town of Silwad, northeast of Ramallah, Israeli forces shot and killed a Palestinian man during a dawn raid in which his
brother was also injured. Their father and brothers were subsequently arrested. This incident was also reported by Middle East
Eye, which identified the killing as occurring during a raid in Silwad.
