- Settler violence in eastern Ramallah villages has been extensively documented, with the Council of Ministers condemning
attacks including the cutting off of hundreds of olive trees in the Tarmsaya plain, north of Ramallah, as part of what it described
as systematic targeting of land and people. The national and Islamic forces of Ramallah & Al-Bireh called for widest public
participation in marches marking the 78th anniversary of the Nakba on May 12, with the central march in Ramallah & Al-Bireh
governorate to be launched in front of the Yasser Arafat shrine toward the city center.
- The Palestinian Prisoners' Society noted that the worsening economic crisis caused by Israel's withholding of Palestinian Authority
clearance revenues has deprived employees of salaries, with the Ramallah & Al-Bireh governor highlighting the impact on
refugees due to the targeting of UNRWA and decline in services. The overall economic situation in the West Bank, including
Ramallah & Al-Bireh, has seen GDP decline by around 13 percent and unemployment rise to approximately 28 percent, with the
Palestinian Minister of Women's Affairs noting that over 650,000 people are unemployed across Palestine and that women face
compounded economic vulnerability.
Hebron
In Hebron governorate, multiple incidents of Israeli military raids, arrests, settler violence, and demolition orders were recorded during
the period of late April to early May 2026, underscoring acute and ongoing protection concerns for the local population.
On 27 April, Israeli forces arrested three children in the town of Beit Ummar, north of Hebron, while simultaneously establishing
checkpoints at the entrances to Hebron and surrounding towns, closing a number of main and secondary roads using iron gates,
concrete blocks, and earth mounds [1734][1738]. On 29 April, Israeli troops raided several neighborhoods in Beit Ummar again,
detaining eight residents including two minors after storming their homes, according to WAFA [1750]. Also on 30 April, Israeli
occupation forces detained 11 citizens in Idhna town, west of Hebron, after storming the town, raiding and searching several homes and
tampering with their contents. Forces also raided several neighborhoods in Hebron city and Sa'ir town to the north, where military
checkpoints were set up and vehicles were stopped and searched [1745].
In a particularly grave incident, a 16-year-old Palestinian teenager was shot in the abdomen by Israeli forces during a raid in the
al-Hawooz area of Hebron city. Local media reported that Israeli forces stormed the area with a large number of military vehicles,
closed the main road, and forced shop owners to shut their businesses, with the raid accompanied by live gunfire and tear gas. The
teenager was taken to the Red Crescent hospital in the city where he was pronounced dead. At least two people were wounded during
the raid, and at least one Palestinian was arrested; the raid also included a strike on the headquarters of a charitable association
[1752][1748].
In a separate incident on 21 April, a vehicle from the security detail of far-right National Security Minister Itamar Ben-Gvir struck and
killed a 16-year-old boy near Hebron [1769].
31
In Arroub refugee camp, north of Hebron, Israeli forces broke in at dawn, prompting violent clashes between Palestinian youths and the
occupying forces. A young man was arrested after his home was raided and searched, and another young man was shot in the leg
during the clashes and taken to Bethlehem hospitals for treatment [1741].
In Hebron governorate, Israeli forces also arrested a municipal election winner from Deir Samt — the warlord who had won the
municipal elections — just days after another winning candidate had been forced to resign. A young man from the southern area of
Hebron was also arrested concurrently with raids on houses in the towns of Sayr and the Shuikhs north of the city [1735].
On the settler violence front, the Palestinian Red Crescent reported that its crew in Hebron dealt with three injuries caused by settler
attacks in Jabal Jalis east of Hebron, including a 71-year-old individual, all taken to hospital [1727][1728][1791]. Separately, four
Palestinians including an elderly woman were injured following a settler attack in Jabal Jalis east of Hebron, with Palestinian Red
Crescent teams transferring three of the injured following a violent assault [1764]. Settlers also attacked agricultural areas in Hebron,
destroyed property, and uprooted dozens of trees [1727][1728].
In Masafer Yatta, south of Hebron, settlers from the Karmiel settlement and surrounding outposts released their livestock under the
protection of Israeli forces onto Palestinian land in Khirbet Rajoum Ali, uprooting and damaging approximately 30 olive trees [1764].
Settlers also released their livestock onto Palestinian land in the Hamroush area, east of the town of Sa'ir, northeast of Hebron,
destroying Palestinian crops. Residents of villages, hamlets, and Bedouin communities in Masafer Yatta and Sa'ir called on local and
international organizations to protect them from these attacks [1764].
Regarding education access, on 13 April Israeli settlers placed razor-wire across the road to a school attended by Palestinian children
from Umm al-Khair village in the south Hebron Hills, blocking students from reaching their school since then. When residents staged a
sit-in protest at the fence, Israeli soldiers fired teargas at them [1785].
On demolition concerns, Israeli authorities issued demolition notices for five homes and a sheep barn in the village of Bireen, southeast
of Hebron, raising concerns over further displacement [1770].
In a development reflecting the broader administrative control situation, planning powers in Hebron have been transferred to the
Israeli Civil Administration, further reducing the actual role of the Palestinian Authority in the area [1771].
A prisoner from Hebron, aged 22, was released from Ramla prison clinic in critical condition after 22 months of detention, having
developed cancer during imprisonment. He was transferred to a hospital in Ramallah. The Palestinian Captives Club reported that he
had been subjected to harsh conditions of detention and a sudden deterioration in his health, and held the Israeli authorities fully
responsible for his condition [1777].
Jenin
In Jenin governorate, Israeli occupation forces conducted multiple raid and arrest operations during the period under review. During
one large-scale incursion, forces stormed the village of Arana, northeast of Jenin city, resulting in the arrest of two youths, according to
local reporting [1735]. In a separate operation, forces stormed the town of Kabatiya, south of Jenin, raiding homes, confiscating
property, and arresting at least two individuals [1735]. A further incursion into Kabatiya involved forces deploying across multiple
neighbourhoods, conducting house searches through the night and into the morning, resulting in the arrest of at least four citizens,
including a mother and her son [1741].
On the settlement expansion front, the Palestinian Ministry of Foreign Affairs on 30 April 2026 condemned an Israeli decision to build 126
new settlement units in the settlement of Sanur, located on land belonging to Jenin Governorate in the northern West Bank
[1780][1767]. The ministry described the move as part of systematic plans to expand and consolidate settlement activity, stating that it
is intended to undermine prospects for peace, displace Palestinians, and deepen the system of apartheid [1780]. UN Assistant
Secretary-General Khaled Khiari separately warned the Security Council of plans by Israeli authorities to build 1,080 new settlement
units within a single month across the West Bank, warning that the expansion threatens Palestinian presence and worsens economic
conditions and insecurity, particularly in refugee camps [1780][1767].
Settler violence also affected the Jenin area, with the Palestinian Council of Ministers condemning land dredging operations in Yamon,
west of Jenin, as part of systematic targeting of Palestinian land and agriculture [1774]. The West Wales Friends of Palestine
additionally reported being unable to run their usual community projects in Jenin camp due to the escalating situation there [1755].
A notable protection case emerged on 1 May 2026, when a Palestinian journalist was freed from Israeli detention after being held
without charge under administrative detention for approximately one year following his arrest at his home in Jenin in April 2025. Upon
release, he showed signs of torture and severe malnutrition, reportedly losing half his body weight due to systematic starvation [1800].
This case highlights the compounding protection and humanitarian concerns facing residents of Jenin, where repeated military raids,
settlement expansion, land attacks, and detention practices continue to generate acute vulnerability.
Nablus
On May 3, 2025, Israeli forces conducted a large-scale military raid on the city of Nablus, entering through the Deir Sharaf checkpoint
and deploying along Asira Street. Forces carried out raids on several shops in the Al-Ein refugee camp and along Sufian Street in the
city's commercial center. During the operation, a 26-year-old Palestinian man was fatally shot in the head outside Ravidia State
Hospital, where he had been waiting for news of the birth of his first child, according to field sources cited by Hamas. Four others were
injured by live ammunition, including two children sustaining wounds to the chest and pelvis, with one young man reported in serious
condition. According to the Palestine Red Crescent Society, approximately 40 people suffered tear gas inhalation, with 10 requiring
hospitalization. Medical sources confirmed that ambulance crews treated at least three live-fire injuries, including two children. The
raid was accompanied by firing of tear gas and stun grenades into busy, pedestrian-crowded streets [1752][1730][1723][1714][1733].
32
On April 23, a 15-year-old was shot dead by Israeli forces in Nablus while on his way home from school, according to Al Jazeera
reporting on the week's events [1769].
On April 27, 2026, Israeli forces conducted raids and detention campaigns in Nablus, detaining several Palestinians, as part of broader
operations across the West Bank and occupied Jerusalem [1734][1738].
On April 28, Israeli forces raided the Askar refugee camp and the village of Beit Iba in Nablus, as part of a wider operation that detained
eight Palestinians across multiple areas, six of whom were former prisoners [1770].
On April 30, 2026, Israeli forces detained five Palestinians in Nablus after storming the city and raiding homes in several neighborhoods
and refugee camps, including Askar and Balata camps. The detainees included three brothers, a young man from the Krum Ashour
area, and another from the Balata refugee camp [1745].
In a separate earlier operation, Israeli forces broke into several neighborhoods of Nablus city, as well as areas in Balata (east) and
Al-Ein camp (west), raiding a number of houses and tampering with their contents, resulting in multiple detentions [1717]. Forces also
arrested a released prisoner after breaking into his home in Balata camp, as well as two brothers from the city center, in a further raid
[1760].
Incursions also extended to the village of Al-Labbin East, south of Nablus [1735]. Israeli forces also sealed the entrances and imposed a
curfew in Madama, south of Nablus [1769].
Settler violence in the Nablus area has been severe. In the village of Jalud, south of Nablus, dozens of settlers attacked residents,
throwing stones and beating citizens before burning down a number of Palestinian homes and properties, causing fear and panic
among the population. Israeli army forces were reportedly deployed around the village during the attack, providing protection to the
settlers. Clashes broke out as Palestinians attempted to defend themselves, and several were injured and taken to hospital [1749].
Three Palestinians were specifically reported injured in Jalud in a settler attack, treated by Palestine Red Crescent Society crews
[1791][1764]. The Palestinian Council of Ministers specifically condemned attacks in the village of Jalud, south of Nablus, describing the
burning of homes and properties as war crimes [1774].
A family in Jalud — the Tobassi family — reported that their home had been burned by settlers and expressed fear of displacement
and property seizure. Young volunteers remained in the burned home to prevent confiscation. The family demanded urgent
international or official protection, the removal of a settler outpost described as the starting point for attacks, and the reopening of
roads closed by settlers and the army [1781].
In the town of Qasra, south of Nablus, settlers attacked poultry farms between Qasra and Jalud, with confrontations erupting in the
area amid firing of tear gas following occupation forces entering the area, according to the mayor of Qasra [1728][1727].
For the second consecutive day, olive trees were uprooted and land was damaged at the main entrance of Barkah village in the
Nablus area, according to reports [1717].
Raids have been ongoing in Nablus for multiple consecutive days, and the Israeli army and border police reported uncovering a
weapons factory and seizing a cache of arms — including an M16 rifle, a pistol, a shotgun, and large quantities of ammunition, as well
as military equipment — during an overnight operation in the area on a Friday preceding the May 3 raid [1752].
Tulkarm
In Tulkarm, Israeli occupation forces conducted multiple arrest and raid operations during the period of late April to early May 2026. On
April 30, a young man was detained after occupation forces stormed his home in the Dhannaba suburb east of the city [1745]. In a
separate operation, occupation forces stormed the suburb of Kataba, east of Tulkarm, and arrested a liberated prisoner and another
individual, following raids on their homes and tampering with their contents [1741]. Forces also raided citizens' homes in Saida town,
north of Tulkarm, and converted a number of them into military barracks [1735]. Additionally, two young men were detained in the city
of Tulkarm after forces broke into their homes and vandalized their contents, while the home of a previously detained individual in the
eastern quarter was also raided, with family members subjected to field investigations [1717].
On the protection of journalists, the Palestinian Journalists' Union reported that one journalist was killed in the city of Tulkarm in the
West Bank since October 7, 2023, making Tulkarm the site of the sole West Bank journalist fatality in that period. The union documented
six journalist fatalities since the beginning of 2026, with Tulkarm specifically noted in cumulative figures [1820][1815][1816].
Qalqilya
- During the reporting period, Israeli forces conducted multiple arrest and raid operations specifically targeting Qalqilya
governorate. On April 30, 2026, Israeli occupation forces stormed the city of Qalqilya, raided several neighborhoods, searched
homes, and detained three young men, according to the Palestinian news agency WAFA [1745]. In a separate operation, Israeli
forces carried out raids in the town of Kafr Kaddoum, located east of Qalqilya city, during which multiple individuals were
arrested, according to the Palestinian Information Centre [1741]. These detention operations in Qalqilya are consistent with the
broader pattern of systematic raids and home searches being conducted across the West Bank during this period, with the
Palestinian Prisoner's Society (PPS) noting that field interrogations, beatings, vandalism of homes, and confiscation of property
routinely accompany such operations as part of what it described as collective punishment targeting all segments of Palestinian
society [1758].
33
Bethlehem
- In the Bethlehem governorate, Israeli occupation forces carried out a series of raids and arrest operations during the period of
late April to early May 2026. On April 27, four Palestinians were detained from different areas of Bethlehem, according to WAFA
[1738][1734]. On April 28, Israeli forces raided Beit Fajjar in Bethlehem as part of a broader arrest campaign, detaining Palestinians
including former prisoners [1770]. In a separate operation, occupation forces broke into the Dheisheh refugee camp and arrested
a journalist, in addition to arresting another individual from the town of Ubeidiya to the east, after raiding and searching their
homes; the latter had reportedly been shot by occupation forces while attempting to reach work in Jerusalem [1735]. The towns
of Beit Sahur, Zawata, Al-Khader, Beit Fajar, Muharralah and Abu Anjim also witnessed military incursions without reported arrests
[1735]. On April 30, a young man was detained in Bethlehem after his home was stormed and searched [1745]. In an additional
incident reported from the Dheisheh camp, a young man was arrested following a raid on his home [1760]. Two youths were also
arrested from the Jabal Handaza area east of Bethlehem city, and another from the Karkfa area in the centre, a resident of Dar
Salah town [1741].
- Settler violence in Bethlehem also intensified during this period. In the "Jabal Harassa" area east of Beit Sahur town, settlers fired
live bullets at Palestinians who were on their land, without reported injuries from gunfire [1717][1749]. In the same area, a young
man was severely beaten by settlers and taken to Beit Jala Government Hospital for treatment [1749]. Local sources reported
that settlers have repeatedly targeted the Harassa area in attempts to seize land and deny Palestinians access to it [1749]. A
young man shot in the leg during clashes in Arroub refugee camp north of Hebron was transported to Bethlehem hospitals for
treatment [1741].
- On a longer-term humanitarian concern, journalist Islam Amraneh — arrested from the Dheisheh camp in Bethlehem — is
identified as the sister of a journalist held under administrative detention, with her arrest representing one of the most recent
cases in an ongoing pattern of press freedom violations [1796]. Bethlehem's Christian community continues to face serious
long-term pressures: the Christian population in the Bethlehem area has declined from approximately 85 percent of the
population in 1947 to roughly 10 percent by 2017, with a 2020 survey of Palestinian Christians identifying occupation-related
conditions — checkpoints, settler attacks, and land confiscation — as the strongest drivers of emigration [1718]. Additionally,
Israeli settlement advertising campaigns are promoting units in the settlement of Nokdim, south of Bethlehem, targeting young
Israeli audiences and reserve soldiers, representing ongoing settlement expansion pressure on Bethlehem-area lands [1788].
Jericho
- According to Arab News, settlers attacked the Bedouin community of Arab Al-Kaabneh, located north of Jericho, during the
reporting period. Settlers stormed the area and threw stones at residents' dwellings, damaging hay bales. No injuries were
reported from this incident. The Al-Baydar Organization for the Defense of Bedouin Rights documented and reported this attack
[1764].
- In a separate reference to the Jericho area, a former British consul general cited the E1 project site as being located on the
Jericho road, describing it as a strategically significant location that would effectively block the northern West Bank from the
southern West Bank [1801]. While this reference is geopolitically framed, it underscores the continued vulnerability of the Jericho
corridor to settlement expansion and territorial fragmentation.
Jerusalem
- During the period of late April to early May 2026, Jerusalem governorate witnessed a severe escalation of Israeli military
operations, detentions, demolitions, and settler activity concentrated in specific neighbourhoods and towns within the
governorate.
- On April 27, Israeli occupation forces launched large-scale raids lasting more than 15 hours in Qalandiya refugee camp, al-Ram,
and Kafr Aqab, all located north of occupied Jerusalem. According to WAFA and the Jerusalem Governorate, more than 35
Palestinians were detained during these operations, with multiple injuries reported including live-fire wounds, beatings, and tear
gas inhalation [1731]. Forces stormed homes, expelled residents, and converted several residential buildings into military outposts
[1725][1731]. Demolition notices were issued against dozens of residential and commercial structures in al-Ram, Kafr Aqab, and
Qalandiya camp under the pretext of construction without permits, according to the Jerusalem Governorate [1762][1725][1719].
The Palestine Liberation Organization's Jerusalem Affairs Department warned that these raids constituted a systematic policy
aimed at fragmenting Palestinian social fabric and imposing coercive security realities around occupied Jerusalem [1719]. The
PLO also reported that the raid on the UNRWA clinic inside Qalandiya camp, including destruction of its entrance, marked a
serious escalation targeting humanitarian infrastructure [1719].
- The Palestinian Prisoner's Society (PPS) reported that on April 27 and 28, Israeli forces detained and interrogated approximately
140 Palestinians from across the West Bank including Jerusalem, among them a woman, children, and former prisoners, with
operations concentrated primarily in al-Ram, Kafr Aqab, and Qalandiya camp [1758]. Most detainees were subsequently
released after field interrogations. The PPS documented accompanying violations including severe beatings, destruction of
homes, confiscation of vehicles, money and jewellery, and use of family members as hostages [1758][1737].
- In al-Ram, north of Jerusalem, two workers were shot by Israeli forces near the separation wall on the same day — one at dawn
while attempting to reach his workplace in Jerusalem, and a second in the evening — both sustaining gunshot wounds to the
legs and transported to hospital by the Palestinian Red Crescent Society [1739][1760]. Two youths from al-Ram were also
detained following raids on their homes, accompanied by the complete closure of the town's entrances and denial of movement
[1717].
34
- On April 30, Israeli police entered the Silwan district south of Al-Aqsa Mosque, setting up a military checkpoint in the Bustan
neighbourhood, issuing fines to vehicles, and detaining one young man while confiscating his vehicle [1745]. In the Al-Thawri
neighbourhood of Silwan, shops shut down as Israeli forces and municipal tax teams raided the area, issuing arbitrary tax
evasion notices against businesses and vehicles [1751]. Also on April 30, Israeli forces assaulted a disabled child and his brother
in Shu'fat refugee camp, northeast of East Jerusalem — the child was briefly detained and physically assaulted despite his visible
medical condition, while his brother sustained facial injuries according to the Jerusalem Governorate and Anadolu Agency
reports [1761][1751]. Additionally, Al-Aqsa Mosque guard Ismail Siyam was detained near Bab al-Asbat and released under
conditions including a seven-day ban from the Old City and a financial fine, while another mosque guard was issued a
six-month ban from Al-Aqsa as part of ongoing measures targeting Islamic Waqf Department employees [1751].
- On the outskirts of Hizma, east of Jerusalem, settler groups attempted to steal livestock from Palestinian herders, reflecting an
increase in attacks on shepherds in the area, according to the Jerusalem Governorate [1751].
- Regarding demolitions and displacement in East Jerusalem, Israeli NGO Ir Amim documented an accelerating demolition
campaign in Silwan's al-Bustan neighbourhood, with 17 homes demolished in 2026 compared to 13 in all of 2025, warning that the
municipality appears to be targeting all 115 homes by October to make way for a park adjacent to the City of David site run by
the settler organisation Elad [1769]. Ir Amim warned that more than 2,000 Palestinians risk displacement in "one of the largest
waves of expulsions in East Jerusalem since 1967." In Silwan's Batn al-Hawa neighbourhood, one family received final eviction
notices for seven apartments to be vacated by May 17, according to the Palestinian Authority's Jerusalem Governorate [1769]. In
Sheikh Jarrah, Israeli authorities approved construction of an 11-storey ultra-Orthodox yeshiva opposite the local mosque,
according to WAFA [1769]. Between March 14 and April 16, Israeli authorities advanced plans for 400 new housing units in East
Jerusalem, according to the UN Assistant Secretary-General Khaled Khiari in a Security Council briefing [1756][1757].
- According to OCHA, an 18-hour Israeli operation in and around Qalandiya camp involved large-scale searches, detentions, and
movement restrictions resulting in injuries, property damage, and temporary displacement, with access to schools, clinics, and
ambulance services also disrupted [1805]. The Palestinian Authority described these raids as part of a policy aimed at
fragmenting the Palestinian social fabric [1762].
- Policies of demolition, confiscation, withdrawal of residency identity documents, and economic pressure continue across Silwan,
Sheikh Jarrah, Jabal al-Makbar, Issawiya, and al-Tur, with the objective of reducing Palestinian demographic presence and
expanding the settlement belt within and around the city, according to Palestinian Information Centre reporting [1713].
Salfit
- In the Salfit governorate, the most directly documented incident during the reporting period involves settler violence in the town
of Jalud (also referred to as Galod/Jaloud), located south of Nablus and within the Salfit area. The Palestinian Red Crescent
Society reported that its crews in Salfit treated three people injured following a violent assault by settlers in Jalud, with settlers —
operating under the protection of the Israeli army — releasing their cattle into olive fields and breaking and uprooting
approximately 30 olive trees [1764][1728][1727]. This attack was part of a broader wave of settler violence documented around
the same period, which also included settlers burning houses and properties in Jalud, causing fear and panic among residents
while Israeli army forces were deployed around the village to provide protection to the attackers [1749]. The attack on Jalud was
specifically condemned by the Palestinian Council of Ministers, which described the burning of Palestinian homes and properties
in the village as part of organized colonial terrorist escalation [1774].
- On the livelihoods and agricultural resilience front, Salfit governorate was named as one of four target areas — alongside Jenin,
Tubas, and Hebron — for the newly launched "Lift-Palestine" agricultural development programme. Implemented by the
Palestinian Ministry of Agriculture in partnership with the We Effect Foundation and funded by the Swedish Consulate in
Jerusalem, the programme runs from July 2025 to June 2029 with a total budget of 7.5 million Shekels, aiming to strengthen the
resilience and livelihoods of agricultural communities facing ongoing attacks on land and farmers [1807].
Tubas
- In Tubas governorate, severe economic hardship continues to affect residents, particularly workers who lost their jobs inside
Israel following the suspension of work permits after October 7, 2023. A resident from Tubas governorate described being
unemployed for more than two and a half years, unable to meet his family's basic needs or support his children's university
education. Despite living in Tubas and the northern Jordan Valley — historically an agricultural area that absorbed large
numbers of seasonal workers — he was also unable to find agricultural work due to tightened controls, checkpoints, and gates
imposed by Israeli authorities [1817].
- On April 30, 2026, Israeli occupation forces detained a young man from Aqaba town in Tubas governorate after summoning him
for interrogation at Salem military camp [1745].
- Settler violence within the Tubas area has also been documented. In the village of Jaloud, southeast of Nablus and bordering the
Tubas governorate area, a family identified as Tobassi faced an organized and sustained settler attack lasting over ten days.
Settlers conducted daily assaults including stone-throwing, destruction of trees, and the release of sheep onto agricultural land
surrounding two homes on the outskirts of the village. The attacks escalated when settlers exploited a hole secretly made in the
house wall to set fire to a vehicle parked inside, with fire and smoke spreading to the second floor and rendering the house
uninhabitable. The family was forced to evacuate women and children to relatives' homes for safety, while the head of household
remained alone to protect his property.
35
His attempts to obtain protection from Palestinian associations, police, and the Israeli army were all unsuccessful [1781].
- A Swedish-funded agricultural development program titled "Living Palestine for Livelihoods, Infrastructure and the
Transformation of Food Systems," launched by the Palestinian Ministry of Agriculture in partnership with the We Effect Foundation
with a total budget of 7.5 million Shekels, is being implemented from July 2025 to June 2029 across the governorates of Jenin,
Salfit, Tubas, and Hebron. The program aims to strengthen the resilience and improve livelihoods of agricultural communities
facing ongoing attacks on land and farmers [1807]. Separately, a UK-based twinning group from Bradford-on-Avon has been
fundraising for language clubs in Tubas and helping to rebuild schools attacked by settlers, reflecting the documented impact of
settler violence on educational infrastructure in the governorate [1755].
Gaza Strip
Gaza
- As of late April to early May 2026, Gaza faces an acute and worsening humanitarian crisis across nearly all dimensions of daily
life, with the population enduring ongoing military violations of the ceasefire, near-total infrastructure collapse, and severe
restrictions on humanitarian access. According to the Gaza Ministry of Health, since the ceasefire of 11 October 2025, the total
number of martyrs has risen to 830 and the total number of casualties to 2,345, while 767 bodies had been recovered from the
rubble, with additional victims remaining unreachable under debris and on roads [1845]. Since 7 October 2023, the cumulative
toll stands at 72,610 killed and 172,448 injured [1845]. The Government Information Office in Gaza documented 377 ceasefire
violations during April 2026 alone, killing 111 civilians and injuring 376 others [1845].
- Specific recent incidents include three police officers killed in a drone strike in Khan Younis on April 21, five people including three
children killed in an airstrike on the courtyard of a mosque in Beit Lahiya on April 22, eight people killed in an attack on a police
vehicle in Khan Younis on April 24, and two police officers killed in a separate attack in Gaza City on the same day [1854]. On
approximately April 26, a woman pregnant with twins and her two young children were killed in artillery shelling near Kamal
Adwan Hospital, and on April 28, a 15-year-old was killed by Israeli forces in Beit Lahiya [1854]. Israeli occupation mechanisms
also targeted eastern neighbourhoods of Jabalia camp and Khan Younis city, and heavy fire was reported east of the Iqlim
al-Tuffah neighbourhood east of Gaza City, with a blow-up operation also carried out in eastern areas of Gaza City [1845]. Israeli
artillery and heavy mechanisms continued targeting Rafah and areas east of Khan Younis [1825].
- According to Action on Armed Violence (AOAV), in 2025 approximately 14,011 civilians were killed or injured by explosive violence
in Gaza, with Gaza City recording the highest civilian casualties at 4,787, followed by Khan Younis at 2,628, Mawasi at 1,120,
Nuseirat at 1,077, and Jabalia at 955 [1856]. Nearly 100% of recorded explosive weapons incidents occurred in populated areas,
with 47% of civilian casualties in urban residential areas, 30% in encampments, and 11% affecting humanitarian infrastructure
[1856].
- Regarding territorial control, as of late April 2026 new Israeli maps issued in mid-March 2026 placed thousands of displaced
Palestinians inside an expanded restricted zone, with the restricted area making up an estimated 11% of Gaza's territory beyond
the "Yellow Line," and together with Israeli-occupied territory, cordoning off nearly two-thirds of Gaza's total area [1821]. As of
March 2026, Israeli forces still control and forbid access to approximately 58% of the Strip for both the population and
humanitarian actors [1886]. In February 2026, WASH humanitarian actors assessed that 43% of WASH facilities were neither
accessible to the population nor to humanitarians, being on the Israeli-controlled side of the yellow line, while an additional 10%
are only accessible if permission is obtained from Israeli authorities [1886].
- The water crisis in Gaza has reached catastrophic levels during April 2026. According to MSF's report "Water as a Weapon"
released on April 28, nearly 90% of Gaza's water and sanitation infrastructure has been damaged or destroyed, including
desalination plants, wells, pipelines and sewage networks [1857][1848]. Gazans sometimes receive less than 6 litres of water per
person per day, far below the internationally recommended minimum of 50 to 100 litres, forcing many families to resort to
contaminated or unsafe sources [1838]. More than 90% of water in Gaza is estimated to be unfit for human consumption due to
salinity and contamination [1838]. Around 60% of families still lack adequate access to clean water [1872][1853]. A recent airstrike
struck NGO workers at a water well in Gaza City, killing one and injuring four others, and operations were also suspended at the Al
Mansoura water filling point after two UNICEF-contracted drivers were killed [1872][1853]. MSF reported that since 1 January 2026,
all its requests for entry of any supplies through the dedicated approval system were denied by Israeli authorities [1886]. MSF
stated it remains one of the main providers of drinking water in Gaza, supplying more than 5.3 million litres per day in the most
recent month, covering minimum needs for over 407,000 people, or roughly one-fifth of the population [1848].
- During September 2025, as Israeli forces conducted military operations on Gaza City, MSF was forced to reduce and then entirely
stop water distribution in the north; drinking and domestic water distributed by MSF in the northern Strip, including Gaza City,
decreased by 95%, going from covering the needs of approximately 268,700 people per day across 232 locations in the second
week of September to fewer than 14,800 people per day across 54 locations by the last week of September [1886]. In May 2025,
"evacuation" orders in Jabalia and Beit Lahia in the North Governorate caused MSF's domestic water distribution from wells and
boreholes to drop from covering minimum daily needs of 155,300 people in 104 locations to 99,100 people in 60 locations within a
two-week period [1886].
- The health sector remains in crisis. According to WHO data, more than 18,500 patients require medical evacuation outside the
Strip, including some 4,000 children [1850]. Fifty-nine percent of essential medicines and 37% of medical supplies are at zero
stock, while hospitals urgently need oxygen stations and rely entirely on generators threatened by fuel shortages [1850].
36
WHO called for the immediate entry of medicines and essential supplies and announced support for the establishment of a new
family health center in northern Gaza where healthcare access remains extremely limited [1859]. Fourteen Gaza doctors were the
subject of a petition by an Israeli rights group to the Israeli top court seeking their release [1840]. The civil defence spokesman for
Gaza, Major Mahmoud Basal, warned of a near-total cessation of humanitarian and relief services due to the continued denial of
petrol, oil and spare parts, with hospitals, ambulances and civil defence all reliant on generators at risk of failure [1839].
- OCHA reported that UN and partner teams visiting displacement sites in eastern Gaza City found around 600 families living in
harsh conditions, sheltering in damaged buildings and tents with little access to clean water and virtually no sanitation services
[1870]. Rodents, insects and untreated waste are widespread, increasing disease risk [1870]. UNRWA reports surging cases of
ectoparasitic infection and chickenpox amid critical shortages of medication and pesticides, with rodent infestations spreading
across residential areas and displacement camps [1835]. Save the Children warned that two in three children are at risk of
infection due to the plague of rats and pests [1833]. Approximately 90% of Gaza's population has been displaced at least once,
with most still in tents or temporary shelters lacking minimum services [1850].
- The ceasefire agreement stipulated 600 trucks per day to enter Gaza, but only 39% of this number has actually entered, with fuel
introduction at only approximately 14.9% of required quantities, according to the Government Information Office in Gaza [1850].
Humanitarian aid flow has been restricted to approximately 20% of what was agreed, with UNRWA and other aid agencies
prevented from fully operating [1835]. The reconstruction of Gaza is estimated to require approximately $71.4 billion over the next
decade, with $26.3 billion needed in the first 18 months alone to restore essential services and rebuild critical infrastructure [1857].
- Small-scale municipal elections took place in Deir el-Balah for the first time since 2006, with a turnout of 23%, which the election
commission attributed to an outdated civil registry reflecting the scale of displacement and death, with the population focused
on survival rather than municipal administration [1854]. In the industrial sector, damage exceeded 95%, with most factories in
eastern areas still under Israeli control, preventing access or rehabilitation and resulting in high unemployment and poverty
rates [1828]. Gaza also faces near-total paralysis in the electricity and communications sectors due to fuel scarcity and
prohibition on generators and spare parts [1828]. A joint EU-UN assessment found that two years of hostilities caused Gaza's
development to leap back by an estimated 77 years [1835].
North Gaza
- In late April and early May 2026, North Gaza continued to experience active hostilities and civilian casualties despite the ceasefire
in force since October 11, 2025. On April 28, 2026, a woman sustained serious injuries from Israeli gunfire in the Egyptian Camp
area near the 17th Street area in the northern Gaza Strip, coinciding with heavy artillery shelling and intense gunfire targeting
areas east of Jabalia refugee camp and Beit Lahia [1847]. On May 3, 2026, a Palestinian young man was shot and killed by Israeli
forces in the al-Hoja Street area of Jabalia refugee camp, raising the total number of Palestinians killed since the October 11, 2025
ceasefire to 832, with total injuries exceeding 2,342 and 767 bodies recovered from rubble [1852]. On the same day, two
additional Palestinians were injured by Israeli gunfire in Jabalia refugee camp [1861].
- Earlier in the reporting period, on April 22, five people including three children were killed in an airstrike on the courtyard of a
mosque in Beit Lahiya. On April 25, a woman pregnant with twins and her two young children were killed in artillery shelling near
Kamal Adwan Hospital. On April 28 (Monday), a 15-year-old was killed by Israeli forces in Beit Lahiya, according to Al Jazeera
reporting [1854]. Occupation mechanisms also targeted eastern neighbourhoods of Jabalia camp as part of continuous military
escalation [1845].
- According to Action on Armed Violence (AOAV), Jabalia was among the hardest-hit towns in Gaza in 2025, recording 955 civilian
casualties from explosive violence, making it the fifth most impacted locality in the Strip for that year [1856]. Beit Lahia was also
listed among the hardest-hit towns in 2025 [1856].
- Regarding water access, MSF reported that in May 2025, Israeli military "evacuation" orders were issued for Jabalia and Beit Lahia
in the North governorate, cutting off MSF access to water distribution points, boreholes and generators. Between May 12–18 and
May 19–25, MSF's domestic water distribution dropped from covering the minimum daily needs of 155,300 people across 104
locations to 99,100 people across 60 locations — a reduction of over one third [1886]. MSF had also planned to repair a borehole
in Beit Lahia and install reverse osmosis units, but evacuation orders and intensified attacks prevented the work from starting,
and the borehole structure was destroyed before repairs could begin [1886]. By mid-March 2025, as orders multiplied for the
north, MSF lost contact with focal points for fuel distribution and could no longer access generators in the area [1886]. MSF's
change in water distribution points between March 16, 2025 and July 20, 2025 reflects the loss of access to North Gaza
governorate entirely [1886].
- WHO reported supporting the establishment of a new family health center in northern Gaza, where access to healthcare remains
extremely limited, providing essential services including noncommunicable disease management, maternal and child health,
routine vaccination, wound care and basic physical rehabilitation [1859].
Deir Al-Balah
- Deir Al-Balah has been among the hardest-hit areas in Gaza in terms of explosive violence, listed alongside Gaza City and
Mawasi as one of the hardest-hit towns in the Strip in 2025, according to Action on Armed Violence (AOAV). Israeli attacks in the
area have continued despite a ceasefire in place since October 2025. Israeli artillery targeted areas east of Deir Al-Balah in
central Gaza, and an Israeli drone strike targeting a group of civilians near Shuhadaa Al-Aqsa Hospital in Deir Al-Balah injured six
Palestinians. A separate drone strike near the Qastal towers east of Deir Al-Balah city killed one Palestinian man.
37
Israeli forces also struck an area near the Qastal towers east of Deir Al-Balah using a drone, and shelling by an Israeli drone in
Deir Al-Balah resulted in at least one fatality. A strike near a hospital in the city of Deir Al-Balah killed one person. Israeli artillery
also targeted areas east of Deir Al-Balah as part of ongoing ceasefire violations [1856][1888][1885][1896][1894][1884][1845].
- On the water and sanitation crisis, the Deir Al-Balah desalination plant — which provides water for up to 400,000 people — was
damaged this period when shrapnel from an Israeli airstrike damaged its power line, forcing it to operate at only 20% capacity on
backup generators for approximately one week due to a lack of spare parts [1893]. Israel's national water company Mekorot
provides water to Deir Al-Balah through one of three pipelines running into Gaza, all of which have sustained damage [1887].
Displaced persons living in camps in Deir Al-Balah have faced acute water shortages, with residents reporting that water truck
deliveries were insufficient to meet camp needs. One patient at an MSF hospital in Deir Al-Balah described needing at least four
water trucks daily to meet the needs of his camp and neighboring tents, while a displaced person in the area stated that water
trucks could not cover demand and that drinking water was the absolute priority for families [1886][1875][1880]. Prices for water
from private providers increased by 500 percent between October 2023 and January 2026, and a shop owner in the Deir Al-Balah
market reported that the price of a 7kg pack of laundry detergent doubled, reflecting a broader affordability crisis for basic
hygiene items [1880][1893].
- MSF relocated some of its reverse osmosis (RO) water production units from Gaza City to Deir Al-Balah and Khan Younis during
September–October 2025, as Israeli forces expanded military operations in Gaza City. Despite this, water production capacity
was severely disrupted: during the week of 15–21 September 2025, MSF could only cover the minimum daily water needs of 46,100
people — a 51% reduction from the previous week — due to forced relocations and operational disruptions [1886]. The forcible
transfer of hundreds of thousands of displaced persons from Gaza City to western Deir Al-Balah further strained already
exhausted WASH resources in the area, as the concentration of people in informal settlements created conditions where proper
infrastructure could not be installed [1886]. MSF reported significant increases in diarrhoea cases in September and October
2025, linked to mass displacement into already-dense informal settlements including in Deir Al-Balah [1886].
- Regarding food security, a World Central Kitchen worker based in Deir Al-Balah reported that the organization, which once
supervised 65 community kitchens, has seen that number more than halved due to limited entry of raw materials, with daily
meal provision reduced from tens of thousands to thousands [1895].
- In a notable political development, Deir Al-Balah held the first municipal elections in Gaza since 2006 on 26 April 2026, marking
the only location in the Gaza Strip where voting took place. Voter turnout was 23%, with the Palestinian Central Elections
Committee attributing the low figure to an outdated civil registry reflecting the scale of displacement and death, and to a
population focused primarily on survival. The Palestinian Authority's Fatah-aligned candidates secured six of 15 contested seats.
Hamas boycotted the elections formally but did not nominate candidates, though one list was widely viewed as aligned with the
group. Some voting took place in tents, and polling ended two hours early due to electricity constraints. The Palestinian election
committee cited widespread destruction as the reason voting could not be held across the rest of Gaza
[1854][1871][1876][1873][1883][1882].
- A fundraising effort by the West Wales Friends of Palestine supported the establishment of a school in a tent in Deir Al-Balah,
which took in around 150 children three days a week, illustrating both severe education disruption and grassroots response to it
[1864]. The area continues to host a large displaced population living in tent camps amid dire humanitarian conditions, with
residents describing overcrowding, insufficient water access, disease spread, and ongoing insecurity as defining features of daily
life [1886][1875][1891].
Khan Younis
- Khan Younis has remained a focal point of acute humanitarian distress and ongoing military activity during the late April to early
May 2026 period, with ceasefire violations continuing to result in civilian casualties. On April 21, three police officers were killed in a
drone strike in Khan Younis, and on April 24, eight people were killed in an attack on a police vehicle in the same area. On April 28,
a 9-year-old child was killed in an Israeli airstrike east of Khan Younis, near the Abu Hamid roundabout, an area reportedly
outside the army's designated deployment lines. Artillery shelling continued targeting the eastern areas of Khan Younis city on
the same day. On May 3, two Palestinians, including a child, were killed by Israeli gunfire in separate incidents in Khan Younis. A
person previously injured by Israeli bombing in the Sheikh Nasser neighbourhood east of Khan Younis city was subsequently
confirmed dead, while another body was recovered from the area around Habi City south of Khan Younis. Israeli naval forces also
shelled the coast of Khan Younis, and a young Palestinian was injured after an Israeli quadcopter drone dropped a bomb in the
Sheikh Nasser area east of Khan Younis. Israeli forces additionally targeted the eastern line area north of Khan Younis and the
eastern neighbourhoods of Khan Younis city with heavy fire from occupation mechanisms. Israel maintains effective control over
large swaths of Khan Younis as part of its broader control of 50 to 59 percent of the Gaza Strip, with artillery targeting Rafah and
the east of Khan Younis as part of ongoing ceasefire violations.
- According to the Action on Armed Violence (AOAV) Explosive Violence Monitor 2025, Khan Younis was the second
worst-impacted area in Gaza in 2025 with 2,628 civilian casualties from explosive violence, behind only Gaza City. A survivor
described Israeli tank shelling on a crowd attempting to collect aid from trucks in Khan Younis on 20 July 2025, in which 59
people were killed and 221 injured.
- The humanitarian situation in Khan Younis is dire across multiple sectors. Hundreds of thousands of displaced persons, including
those forcibly transferred from Gaza City in September–October 2025 to already-dense informal settlements in Khan Younis and
Deir al-Balah, have placed immense pressure on exhausted resources.
38
According to MSF, in October 2025 alone, their Al-Attar and Al-Mawasi primary healthcare centres, both located in the south of
Khan Younis governorate, treated 1,077 cases of non-bloody diarrhoea and 44 cases of bloody diarrhoea, driven by overcrowding
and contaminated water use. MSF also reported gunfire at one of its water trucking distribution points in Khan Younis on 23
August, during which a civilian was shot in the ribs and another in the hand, two MSF staff took cover, and nearby tented
structures housing displaced people sustained damage; water distribution was subsequently suspended. During an Israeli forces
incursion on Khan Younis, gunfire was also directed at an MSF water truck while people were filling jerrycans, and an Israeli tank
fired at a clearly identified MSF staff shelter in south Khan Younis, killing two colleagues' family members and injuring six people.
When MSF constructed a new reverse osmosis system in Khan Younis, it took one month to source the necessary borehole
equipment on the local market due to supply blockades.
- On the food security front, a displaced resident from Jabalia relocated to Al-Mawasi in Khan Younis reported total dependence
on community kitchens, with meal delivery having become sporadic and forcing a four-kilometre daily walk to access food. On
May 1, hundreds of Palestinian workers marched in Khan Younis to demand their rights to work, food, and shelter, in a march
commemorating World Labour Day. A trade union member from Khan Younis described widespread unemployment and famine
and called on international labour bodies to support Palestinian workers. Residents of Khan Younis tent encampments described
the situation as the start of a new war of reconstruction, with infrastructure including electricity, water, sewage, schools, and
streets all requiring rebuilding.
- Regarding shelter and health, as part of an urgent plan in partnership with UNDP, the Ministry of Public Works and Housing was
working to equip tents and additional housing units in Khan Younis to alleviate the shelter crisis, with only 2,000 housing units
having entered the entire Gaza Strip — less than 1% of actual need. Residents and displaced persons in Khan Younis camps,
including in Al-Mawasi, reported severe rat and flea infestations, with one resident stating that rats jump over children at night
and another in Mawasi Khan Younis reporting that all camps suffer from stinging insects causing severe itching among children.
The Director of the Children's Section of Nasser Medical Complex warned of worsening malnutrition, receiving 75 children in a
single working day, with roughly half suffering from moderate malnutrition, high rates of anaemia, and widespread
gastrointestinal and skin infections. KSrelief distributed 1,210 food baskets to vulnerable groups in Khan Younis, benefiting 7,260
people, as part of Saudi Arabia's broader humanitarian response.
Rafah
- In Rafah, MSF had supported the rehabilitation of a borehole and installed a reverse osmosis (RO) unit capable of producing
enough drinking water for almost 16,000 people per day. After rapidly intensifying Israeli military activities, MSF was forced to
leave the area on 24 March 2025. MSF has not been able to access or operate this infrastructure since, as the zone remains under
Israeli military control. Satellite images confirmed that the MSF water infrastructure in Rafah has been completely destroyed and
the area flattened [1886].
- At the end of March 2025, following the collapse of the first ceasefire, an evacuation order was issued for the entire Rafah
governorate. As of March 2026, the area remains inaccessible to both the population and WASH actors. MSF had also installed a
medium-sized RO desalination and water treatment unit distributing water to the population at multiple access points in Rafah,
but was not given time to retrieve its equipment before the order took effect. Satellite imagery shows MSF's installation was
completely destroyed, and the area has been reduced to a flattened desert of rubble [1886].
- According to MSF's report "Water as a Weapon," the Rafah governorate has been effectively inaccessible since the end of March
2025, with no humanitarian WASH operations possible in the area. This loss of critical water production assets directly deprived
thousands of residents and displaced persons of their only safe water source [1886].
- On approximately 28 April 2026, the Palestinian Red Crescent Society announced the evacuation of 47 travelers through the
Rafah border crossing, including 24 patients and 23 companions, as part of medical evacuations coordinated by the World
Health Organization (WHO). The Society's ambulances transported the travelers and ensured their safe arrival, as part of its
ongoing humanitarian response to facilitate the movement of patients, the wounded, and their companions for treatment
outside the Gaza Strip [1832]. A separate report noted that around 700 patients had left Gaza for treatment abroad since the
limited reopening of the Rafah crossing on 2 February, while more than 18,000 others remained in need of medical evacuation
[1841].
- Restrictions on movement through the Rafah crossing were identified as a key driver of the humanitarian crisis, particularly
affecting patients requiring treatment outside Gaza. According to the Gaza Ministry of Health, more than 20,000 patients and
wounded people are currently waiting to travel abroad for medical treatment, with only 154 children allowed to leave Gaza since
the crossing partially reopened in February [1892]. The Government Information Office in Gaza specifically cited the agreed
opening of the Rafah crossing as among the ceasefire provisions not being honored by Israel [1850].
- A fisherman was injured by Israeli naval fire in the Rafah sea in the southern Gaza Strip, in one of the continued ceasefire
violations reported in the area [1897][1896]. Israeli artillery was also reported shelling the western areas of Rafah [1894]. Israeli
artillery and heavy mechanisms were further reported targeting Rafah and areas south of the Gaza Strip as part of a broader
pattern of ceasefire violations [1825].
- According to the Action on Armed Violence (AOAV) Explosive Violence Monitor 2025, Rafah was recorded among the hardest-hit
towns in Gaza during 2025, with between 51 and 100 explosive weapon incidents recorded in the area, contributing to the overall
toll of 14,011 civilians killed or injured across the Gaza Strip that year [1856]. Israel is reported to maintain effective control over
large swaths of Rafah as part of its broader control of 50 to 55 percent of the Strip, including systematic infrastructure
destruction in controlled areas [1835].
